## Automatic Configuration (Recommended)

Add Sentry automatically to your app with the [Sentry wizard](https://docs.sentry.io/platforms/react-native/#install) (call this inside your project directory).

```bash
npx @sentry/wizard@latest -i reactNative --saas --org anton-m3 --project collectables
```

The Sentry wizard will automatically patch your project with the following:

 Configure the SDK with your DSN
 Add source maps upload to your build process
 Add debug symbols upload to your build process

##

[DONE: 2026-05-24] [est: 1100] - VM-F: SelectableItemRow memoization end-to-end so React.memo on the row can actually skip re-render work for unchanged rows in selection mode. Three coordinated changes: (1) `components/selectable-item-row.tsx` — wrapped the export in `React.memo(function SelectableItemRow(...))` (named function for React DevTools) and imported `memo` from "react". Without the memo the row would still re-run its entire render on every parent re-render even with a stable renderItem closure. (2) `app/collection/[id].tsx` — added `useCallback` to the React import list; promoted `toggleSelect` from a plain function to `useCallback(..., [])` (empty deps because `setSelectedIds` is React-stable) so the `onToggle` prop the row receives is referentially equal across renders, letting the row memo's shallow prop compare actually skip; hoisted the selection-mode FlatList's inline `({ item }) => (<SelectableItemRow .../>)` arrow into a top-level `renderSelectableRow = useCallback(({ item }) => (<SelectableItemRow item={item} selected={selectedIds.has(item.id)} onToggle={toggleSelect} />), [selectedIds, toggleSelect])`. Pre-VM-F the inline arrow allocated a fresh closure every parent render, defeating the row memo. (3) Selection-mode FlatList JSX now passes `renderItem={renderSelectableRow}` + `extraData={selectedIds}` — the `extraData` is the key piece that tells FlatList's virtualization to consider re-renders when the selection set mutates while `data={visibleItems}` reference is stable (the array is memoized upstream by `useChunkedList`). Tests: new `__tests__/collection-detail-vm-f-selection-memo.test.ts` (5 cases) pins each leg independently — row export is `memo(...)`, `memo` is imported, `toggleSelect` is `useCallback(..., [])`, `renderSelectableRow` is `useCallback` with `selectedIds`+`toggleSelect` deps, FlatList uses the hoisted callback (no inline arrow regression), FlatList passes `extraData={selectedIds}`. Updated `__tests__/collection-detail-vm-e-selection-flatlist.test.ts` and `__tests__/collection-detail-chunked-render.test.ts` to be VM-F-aware (the inline `renderItem={(...) => <SelectableItemRow>}` pattern is no longer required since the JSX moved to a hoisted callback, but the `<FlatList data={visibleItems}>` + `<SelectableItemRow>` shape is still pinned). Verified: `tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 1375/1375 pass, `npm run build` succeeds.

Validation is lenient by design: language codes are lower-cased + trimmed; currency codes are upper-cased and validated against the ISO 4217 `^[A-Z]{3}$` shape; invalid tokens (missing colon, empty key, currency too short/long/numeric) are silently dropped so a typo never crashes the app or blocks the rest of the override from applying. Last value wins on duplicate language keys (`ru:RUB,ru:EUR` → `EUR`). `getDefaultCurrencyForLanguage` and `languageCurrencyMap` exports are unchanged — call sites in `app/create.tsx`, `app/item/[id].tsx`, and `components/currency-input.tsx` pick up the override transparently. [DONE: 2026-05-21] [est: 1100] - Forward subscription events from one shared `RealtimeClient` channel into multiple consumers (chat inbox + marketplace listings) instead of re-subscribing per-screen. Today every screen creates its own channel; if 3 tabs are open the same UPDATE row arrives 3×. A small fan-out subscriber registry on top of `getSharedRealtimeClient` would deduplicate. — New pure `lib/realtime-channel-registry.ts` exporting `subscribeShared<TPayload>(client, topic, configure, onPayload, onStatusChange?)`. Pure module (no react-native imports) — can be exercised under `node --test` directly via a fake `RealtimeClient`. Backed by a `WeakMap<RealtimeClient, Map<string, Entry>>` so a stale client (post-`closeSharedRealtimeClient`) gets a fresh entry map without leaking memory; the per-client keying also isolates two different clients sharing the same topic name. Ref-counted: first subscriber for `(client, topic)` constructs the channel + runs `configure(channel, emit)` once + calls `.subscribe(...)` once; subsequent subscribers just append their handler to the fan-out `Set` and have any currently-known `connected` status replayed to them immediately (so a late joiner doesn't have to wait for the next reconnect transition). The channel is only removed via `client.removeChannel` when the *last* handler unsubscribes — `unsubscribe` is idempotent so double-calls don't double-remove. Per-handler `try/catch` isolation in both the payload fan-out and the status fan-out so one buggy consumer can't kill the socket. `removeChannel` returns a Promise — its rejection is swallowed via a `.then(undefined, () => undefined)` so a flaky network teardown doesn't surface as an `unhandledRejection`. `lib/supabase-chat.ts:subscribeToInbox` and `lib/supabase-marketplace.ts:subscribeToListings` refactored to thread through `subscribeShared` (deleted their bespoke `client.channel(topic)` + `.subscribe` + `removeChannel` blocks; the `inboxChannelTopic`/`inboxFilter`/`POSTGRES_CHANGES`/`INSERT` shape + the `captureException(err, { context: "...handler" })` per-handler guard are preserved so the existing `sentry-capture-wiring.test.ts` + `supabase-chat-wiring.test.ts` continue to pass). `subscribeToTyping` is intentionally NOT migrated — its presence-tracking semantics (per-user `.track({ typing })` + presence sync/join/leave) don't fit the per-topic fan-out shape. `RealtimeChannel` import dropped from `supabase-marketplace.ts` (no longer used after the inline channel construction was deleted). Tests: new `__tests__/realtime-channel-registry.test.ts` (17 cases / 2 suites) — 12 behavioural cases against a fake client (configure-runs-once, fan-out across N consumers, status replay, late-joiner status replay, isolated handler exceptions, ref-counted release, idempotent unsubscribe, fresh channel after full-cycle release, per-topic isolation, per-client isolation, async `removeChannel` rejection doesn't throw out of unsubscribe) plus 5 structural cases (chat + marketplace route through `subscribeShared`, no longer call `client.channel(...)` directly; registry exports + `WeakMap<RealtimeClient` typing + ≥3 try/catch isolation blocks). Verified: `tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 1091/1091 pass (was 1074), `npm run build` succeeds.

Snapshot is a `Map<topic, connected>` kept in sync with entry lifecycle: a new topic enters as `false` (so consumers can show "connecting" before `SUBSCRIBED` fires), transitions to `true` when `channel.subscribe` reports `SUBSCRIBED`, and is dropped from the snapshot when the last subscriber releases (mirrors the existing ref-counted channel removal so a post-sign-out `closeSharedRealtimeClient` correctly resets the surface back to `idle`). Listeners receive a fresh shallow copy of the snapshot on every change — guards against a consumer stashing the reference and silently observing later mutations. Per-listener `try/catch` isolation so a buggy consumer can't block the rest of the fan-out. Repeat subscribers on the same topic (which the registry already collapses to one channel) do NOT re-emit a duplicate snapshot since no underlying status changed. `__resetChannelRegistryForTests` now also clears `statusSnapshot` and `statusListeners` so tests start with the documented empty-initial-snapshot invariant. [DONE: 2026-05-22] [est: 1400] - next to cost in item add select of currency, and implement functionallity of converting currencies for total collection cost (pich any free solution for currency rates) — The currency selector next to cost already shipped in `app/create.tsx` (lines 260-268, `currencySelector` Pressable opening the `CURRENCIES` sheet); each item persists `costCurrency: string | null` alongside `cost: number | null`. This task closed the second half: the codebase summed item costs as raw numbers without converting between currencies, so a collection containing 100 USD + 100 EUR rendered as "200" with no unit. **Free rates source:** `https://open.er-api.com/v6/latest/USD` — no API key, ~160 ISO 4217 currencies, daily refresh (matches the ECB cadence aggregators republish), CORS-enabled (works in the GitHub Pages web build without a proxy). Picked over `frankfurter.dev` (only ~31 currencies — would silently skip RUB/BYN/KZT for our Russian-speaking userbase) and `exchangerate.host` (recently moved to paid tier). **New pure module `lib/currency-rates.ts`:** `parseRatesResponse(raw, now)` (validates `result === "success"`, filters non-ISO/non-positive/non-finite values, always injects `USD: 1` even when upstream omits the self-rate, returns frozen payload), `convertAmount(amount, from, to, rates)` (USD-anchor math: `amount * rates[to] / rates[from]`; returns null when either currency missing or non-finite — callers surface "conversion unavailable" rather than displaying a wrong number), `isStale(payload, now, ttl)` (24h default, `>=` boundary so the equality case re-fetches), `sumConverted(entries, displayCurrency, rates)` (returns `{ total, converted, skipped }` so the UI can show partial-total hints), plus AsyncStorage wrappers `getCachedRates` / `setCachedRates` / `fetchUsdRates(fetchImpl)` (injectable for tests) and the orchestrator `loadCurrencyRates({ forceRefresh, fetchImpl, ttlMs, now })`. **Storage:** added `CURRENCY_RATES_KEY = "collectables-currency-rates-v1"` to `lib/storage-keys.ts` and wired into `clearAllUserData` so signing out drops the cache. **Context integration (`lib/collections-context.tsx`):** added `displayCurrency` state (seeded from `getDefaultCurrencyForLanguage(language)`, hydrated from `getUserPreferredCurrency()` on mount), `currencyRates: UsdRates | null` state, two `useEffect`s (currency hydration + rates load on mount), and `refreshCurrencyRates()` for force-refresh. Changed `getCollectionTotalCost` signature: was `(id) => number`, now `(id) => { amount, currency, converted, skipped }` — uses `sumConverted` when rates are loaded, falls back to raw-summation (treating all items as already in `displayCurrency`) when rates are still loading so first paint doesn't crash. **Consumer updates:** `components/collection-card.tsx` accepts new `totalCostCurrency?: string` prop and renders `{formatCostAmount(amount)} {currency}`; `app/index.tsx` (3 call sites — owned/friends/subscribed), `app/collections-feed.tsx`, `app/profile/[id].tsx` (5 total call sites across 3 files) destructure `{amount, currency}` and forward both; `app/collection/[id].tsx` summary card replaced the inline `allItems.reduce(...)` with `getCollectionTotalCost(activeCollection.id)` + `formatCostAmount(amount)` so the converted total + currency display lives on the detail page too. New `lib/format-cost.ts` (`formatCostAmount(amount)`): rounds to 2 decimals, drops trailing zeros, inserts thousands separators — pure (no Intl) so it tests in node. **Tests:** new `__tests__/currency-rates.test.ts` (37 cases / 7 suites): `parseRatesResponse` (7) — frozen-payload happy path, USD self-rate injection, `result !== success` rejection, null/non-object/non-array payload rejection, non-numeric/NaN/Inf/zero/negative-rate filtering, non-ISO-4217 key filtering, empty-survivor null return; `convertAmount` (8) — identity, USD→non-USD, non-USD→USD, non-USD→non-USD cross, unknown-from/to null, non-finite amount null, zero/negative rate null; `isStale` (4) — null payload, in-window, `>=` boundary, default-TTL pinning; `sumConverted` (4) — empty, mixed-currency sum, unknown-currency skipping, same-currency no-op; endpoint+storage (4) — pinned URL, 24h TTL constant, storage key value, `clearAllUserData` includes it; structural (4) — `loadCurrencyRates`'s cache-then-fetch flow, `fetchUsdRates` try/catch wrapping `parseRatesResponse`, `setCachedRates` JSON shape, `getCachedRates` defensive filtering; context-wiring (5) — imports, mount-effect, return shape, fallback branch, `displayCurrency` / `refreshCurrencyRates` typing. Plus new `__tests__/format-cost.test.ts` (4 cases) — integer formatting, decimal rounding/trailing-zero drop, thousands separators, non-finite guard. Verified: `npm test` 1201/1201 pass (was 1160), `npm run build` succeeds, `tsc --noEmit` clean. **MANUAL-TASKS.md updates:** none — the API is keyless and CORS-enabled, no Supabase migration required, no env var. **Limitations / follow-ups** (logged in `.suggestions.md`): (1) the listing form in `app/item/[id].tsx` and item edit don't yet surface the currency picker (only create does); (2) the marketplace listing flow still inlines `costCurrency` without conversion; (3) failed rate loads degrade silently — a tiny "rates unavailable" pill would let power users tell when they're seeing raw sums instead of converted ones; (4) `sumConverted` returns 0 + `skipped > 0` when ALL items are in unknown currencies — the UI could disambiguate this from "no items" with a different empty-state; (5) the API supports per-base endpoints — switching to the user's preferred base would avoid round-tripping through USD for the common all-EUR case (~0.5% precision win).

## Collection page chunked loading (decomposed from "items should load via chunks to prevent iOS memory leaks")

Context: `app/collection/[id].tsx` is wrapped in a `NestableScrollContainer` (so its outer scroll is a `ScrollView`, not a virtualized list) and has 3 mutually-exclusive render branches for items — (a) owner + drag mode → `NestableDraggableFlatList data={items}` (nested in a ScrollView, so no real virtualization), (b) owner + selection mode → plain `items.map(<SelectableItemRow>)` (unwindowed), (c) viewer/read-only → masonry `items.filter().map(<ItemCard compact>)` across two columns (unwindowed). All three mount every item-card (and its remote image) up-front, which is the iOS memory hot-spot the user flagged. Plan: ship a pure pagination helper first, wire it into all 3 branches behind one "Load more" CTA (minimum viable per the user — pagination is the explicit fallback), then optionally graduate to true `FlatList` windowing once the pagination is proven.

[DONE: 2026-05-23] [est: 600] Add a pure `useChunkedList<T>(items: T[], pageSize = 20): { visibleItems: T[]; hasMore: boolean; loadMore: () => void; reset: () => void }` hook in new `lib/use-chunked-list.ts`. — New `lib/use-chunked-list.ts` exports `useChunkedList<T>`, the `ChunkedList<T>` result type, `DEFAULT_CHUNK_PAGE_SIZE = 20`, and two pure helpers (`clampCount`, `resolvePageSize`) carved out so the slice math is unit-testable without React. Hook seeds count via `useState<number>(() => safePageSize)` (lazy initializer — eager form would re-eval on every render), memoizes the slice via `useMemo(() => items.slice(0, clampCount(...)), [items, count, safePageSize])`, and resets the window via `useEffect(() => setCount(safePageSize), [items, safePageSize])` keyed on the *reference* of `items` so a filter swap (new array) snaps back to one page (without this a user who scrolled to "show 200" then filtered down to 3 would see 200 worth of stale rows). `hasMore` compares `items.length` against the slice length (not the raw count) so the CTA never lingers after `clampCount` pins the count to total. `loadMore` clamps via `clampCount(current + safePageSize, safePageSize, items.length)` so it can't overshoot. `resolvePageSize` mirrors the `resolveInterval` pattern from `lib/use-now.ts`: non-finite/non-positive/fractional `pageSize` falls back to `DEFAULT_PAGE_SIZE = 20`. `clampCount` treats `NaN`/`<=0` `current` as "fall back to one page", `Infinity` and overshoot as "pin to total" — semantically `Infinity` means "show everything", which is the natural pin behaviour. **Contract:** callers MUST pass a stable `items` reference when the underlying list doesn't change (memoize `.filter()` outputs with `useMemo`) — otherwise the identity-reset effect fires every render and `loadMore` becomes a no-op; documented in the module JSDoc. Tests in new `__tests__/use-chunked-list.test.ts` (18 cases / 3 suites): `clampCount` — inside-range, overshoot pin (incl. `Math.min(Infinity, total) = total`), NaN/0/negative fallback, total < pageSize, empty list, fractional floor; `resolvePageSize` — positive integers pass through, NaN/0/negative/Infinity fall back to default, fractional floors, default pinned at 20; structural — react imports (`useState`/`useEffect`/`useMemo` via 3 distinct regexes since import order isn't guaranteed), lazy initializer (`useState<number>(() => safePageSize)`), useMemo around `items.slice`, identity-reset `useEffect` deps `[items, safePageSize]` (the THE invariant), `loadMore` threads through `clampCount`, `safePageSize` threads through `resolvePageSize`, `hasMore` compares against slice length not raw count, `ChunkedList<T>` type export. Verified: `npm test` 1241/1241 pass (was 1223), `npm run build` succeeds, `npx tsc --noEmit` clean.

[DONE: 2026-05-23] [est: 1200] Wire `useChunkedList` into `app/collection/[id].tsx`. — One `useChunkedList(items)` call at the top of the component (right after the `applyItemFilters` `useMemo`) — *single* shared instance so all 3 render branches read from the same windowed slice. Drag-mode `NestableDraggableFlatList` `data={visibleItems}`; selection-mode `selectList` maps `visibleItems`; viewer-masonry both columns filter `visibleItems` (not `items`). **Drag-end remap** (the critical edge): `onDragEnd` receives `data` (reordered visible slice); without remap, `reorderItemsInCollection` would re-sortOrder items 21..N to 0..N-1 alongside the visible slice and shuffle them relative to each other. Fix: `const visibleIds = new Set(visibleItems.map(i => i.id)); const tail = items.filter(i => !visibleIds.has(i.id)); reorderItemsInCollection(id, [...data, ...tail].map(i => i.id));` — only the visible slice moves, the tail keeps its existing order. `EmptyState` branches deliberately keep `allItems.length === 0` / `items.length === 0` gates (NOT `visibleItems.length`) — the window is bounded, but pinning the original condition closes the regression vector via a structural assertion. Selection audit: no "Select all" UI exists; `selectedIds` is a `Set<string>` updated per-row, independent of the visible window. Bulk-bar `selectedCount` iterates `selectedIds.size` — unaffected. Added `loadMore` / `loadMoreText` styles (CARD_BG_3 bg + AMBER_SOFT border + MUTED_3 text — values inline today, will collapse onto design-tokens in the existing migration sweep) gated on `hasMore`; CTA renders below the list with `accessibilityRole="button"` + `accessibilityLabel={t("loadMoreItemsA11y", { count })}` + `accessibilityHint={t("loadMoreItemsHint")}`. Verified: `npm test` + `npm run build` + `npx tsc --noEmit` all clean.

## Virtualization migration (decomposed from "Stretch: replace NestableScrollContainer with FlatList")

Context: chunked pagination already shipped (caps mount count), so the original "stretch" goal of true row-recycling is now incremental. Original task spread three concerns: (1) hoist Hero+filters into a ListHeaderComponent, (2) swap masonry for `FlatList numColumns={2}`, (3) decide drag-mode fate. Decomposed bottom-up so each sub-task ships independently — pure helper first, then refactor on top of it, then UI swap.

[DONE: 2026-05-24] [est: 350] **VM-A — pure masonry distribution helper.** Add a pure `distributeIntoMasonryColumns<T>(items: T[], columnCount = 2): T[][]` in new `lib/masonry.ts` that round-robins items into N columns (column 0 gets indices 0,N,2N…; column 1 gets 1,N+1,2N+1… — same shape as the current `.filter((_, i) => i % 2 === 0/1)` pair in `app/collection/[id].tsx`). — New `lib/masonry.ts` exports `distributeIntoMasonryColumns<T>(items, columnCount = 2): T[][]` + the pure `resolveColumnCount(columnCount): number` clamp. The distributor allocates an `Array.from({ length: safeCount }, () => [])` of empty columns up-front so an empty `items` input still produces `[[], []]` (the masonry caller needs the column shell to take its layout slot even when there are no items — empty-state placeholder lives outside the grid). The single `for` loop indexes via `i % safeCount` and pushes into the column directly so items keep their input reference (not cloned) — `ItemCard` downstream is memo-equality sensitive. `resolveColumnCount` clamps non-finite / `<1` / fractional column counts to a floor of 1, mirroring the `resolvePageSize` / `resolveInterval` defensive-clamp pattern in `lib/use-chunked-list.ts` and `lib/use-now.ts`; a `0` or NaN columnCount would otherwise make `i % safeCount` produce NaN and silently corrupt the distribution. **Contract pinned in tests:** input array is not mutated (the path is sometimes given a memoized `visibleItems` reference shared with other render branches — mutating it would corrupt sibling views), and items are returned by reference (cloning would invalidate downstream memoization). New `__tests__/masonry.test.ts` (12 cases / 2 suites): `resolveColumnCount` — positive ints pass through, `0`/`-1`/`-100`/`NaN`/`±Infinity` fall back to 1, fractional values floor; `distributeIntoMasonryColumns` — empty input across 1/2/3 columns, single-column passthrough, 2-col exact multiple `[0,1,2,3,4,5]→[[0,2,4],[1,3,5]]` (the legacy `.filter((_,i)=>i%2===N)` shape — regression here would shuffle the collection-detail masonry), 2-col uneven trailing-to-column-0, 3-col round-robin, default `columnCount=2` when omitted, non-positive/non-finite fall-through routes via `resolveColumnCount` (asserts the helper actually wires through it instead of crashing on `i % 0`), input not mutated, item identity preserved (returns references), single-item-across-multiple-columns, and column ordering preserved (column 0 is 0,2,4 in ascending index order so the visual top-to-bottom flow is correct). Verified: `npm test` 1339/1339 pass (was 1327 — 12 new cases), `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` succeeds. Confirmed via repo scan (`grep "i % 2 === " app/ components/`) the inline modulo pattern lives only in the one masonry call site (VM-B will replace it) — no related bug to fix.

## In-collection search + sort (decomposed from the two parent tasks above)

Both extend the existing `ItemFilters` / `applyItemFilters` shape in `components/item-filters.tsx` and surface in the filter sheet, so the decomposition splits each parent into "pure logic" (testable without React) and "UI + i18n" (the visible glue). The drag-corruption defense for sort is intentionally bundled with the UI sub-task because the gate lives in `app/collection/[id].tsx`, not in the pure helper.

[DONE: 2026-05-23] [est: 300] **A — Pure search logic.** — Extracted the filter helpers from `components/item-filters.tsx` into a new pure module `lib/item-filters.ts` (no React Native imports) so the matchers can be unit-tested under `node --test` without mocking `@expo/vector-icons` — the component file now re-exports `applyItemFilters` / `EMPTY_FILTERS` / `ItemFilters` for existing callers (`@/components/item-filters`) so no consumer paths broke. Added `query: string` to `ItemFilters` (default `""` in `EMPTY_FILTERS`); `applyItemFilters` filters by case-insensitive `item.title.includes(needle)` with the needle trimmed+lowercased ONCE outside the per-item loop (500 items × 2 `.toLowerCase()` per item = 1000 calls saved per pass). `countActiveFilters` increments for non-whitespace `f.query` only — a whitespace-only query is a no-op per `applyItemFilters` and must not inflate the badge. Tests in new `__tests__/item-filters-query.test.ts` (9 cases / 2 suites): empty/whitespace queries are no-ops, case-insensitive matching, trim surrounding whitespace, substring not whole-word, no-match returns `[]`, AND composition with price filters; plus `EMPTY_FILTERS.query === ""` + `ItemFilters` shape pin. [DONE: 2026-05-23] [est: 500] **C — Pure sort logic.** Extend `ItemFilters` with `sort: "default" | "name-asc" | "name-desc"` (default `"default"`). New pure `applySortMode(items, sort)` helper. — Added `ItemSortMode = "default" | "name-asc" | "name-desc"` to `lib/item-filters.ts`; `ItemFilters.sort: ItemSortMode` is required (so TS catches any caller that builds an `ItemFilters` literal without it). `EMPTY_FILTERS.sort = "default"`. `applySortMode(items, "default")` returns the input array reference unchanged (identity path — no allocation, preserves React-memo equality when no sort is active). `applySortMode(items, "name-asc")` clones via `[...items].sort((a, b) => a.title.localeCompare(b.title, undefined, { sensitivity: "base", numeric: true }))` — `sensitivity: "base"` collates accented chars next to their base letter (matters for ru/be/pl/de/es), `numeric: true` puts "Item 2" before "Item 10". `name-desc` reuses the same comparator + `sorted.reverse()`. `countActiveFilters` increments by 1 for any non-`default` sort. `applySortMode` + `ItemSortMode` re-exported from `components/item-filters.tsx` so existing call sites (`@/components/item-filters`) stay unbroken. Tests in new `__tests__/item-filters-sort.test.ts` (13 cases / 2 suites): `default` returns input reference (identity), `name-asc` sorts A→Z, `name-desc` sorts Z→A, case-insensitive `"Apple" < "banana"`, accented `"élite"` near `"elite"`, numeric-aware `"Item 2"` before `"Item 10"`, name-desc is strict reverse of name-asc, NO mutation of input array (pure-helper contract), empty input returns empty for every mode, `EMPTY_FILTERS.sort === "default"`, `countActiveFilters` does NOT increment for default, DOES increment for name-asc/name-desc, composes additively with other filters. Verified: `npm test` 1311/1311 pass (was 1298), `npx tsc --noEmit` clean, `npm run build` succeeds.

[DONE: 2026-05-23] [est: 600] **D — Sort UI + drag-mode gate + i18n.** Added the sort row to `components/item-filters.tsx` (3 pill chips: Default / A→Z / Z→A) styled via a sibling `sortChip`/`sortChipActive`/`sortChipText`/`sortChipTextActive` family that mirrors the existing `filterButton` pill shape (CARD_BG_3 bg + AMBER_SOFT border idle, HERO_DARK bg+border + TEXT_ON_DARK_5 text active). Chip writes via `setDraft({ ...draft, sort: opt.mode })` so other in-flight draft state (price/date/source/query/photos) is preserved. `app/collection/[id].tsx`: imported `applySortMode` from `@/components/item-filters` and split the items pipeline into two memos — `filteredItems = useMemo(applyItemFilters(allItems, itemFilters), [allItems, itemFilters])` followed by `items = useMemo(applySortMode(filteredItems, itemFilters.sort), [filteredItems, itemFilters.sort])`. **Sort-memo deps are `[filteredItems, itemFilters.sort]`** — depending on the full `itemFilters` object would re-sort on every priceFrom keystroke even though the sort mode hasn't changed. The two-memo split gives the chunked-list hook a stable `items` reference whenever neither filters nor sort change, preserving the `useChunkedList` identity-reset semantics. **Critical drag-corruption gate:** the `isOwner && !selectionMode` branch now also requires `itemFilters.sort === "default"` — when the user picks A→Z or Z→A, the `NestableDraggableFlatList` branch falls through to the masonry view (the existing `else` arm) even for owners, so `onDragEnd` can never fire while alphabetically sorted and silently re-write `sortOrder` based on the visible (alphabetical) order. 4 new i18n keys (`sortLabel` / `sortDefault` / `sortNameAsc` / `sortNameDesc`) added to the `en` source table + localized overrides in ru ("Сортировка"/"По умолчанию"/"А → Я"/"Я → А"), be ("Сартаванне"/"Па змаўчанні"/"А → Я"/"Я → А"), pl ("Sortowanie"/"Domyślnie"/"A → Z"/"Z → A"), de ("Sortierung"/"Standard"/"A → Z"/"Z → A"), es ("Orden"/"Predeterminado"/"A → Z"/"Z → A"). `countActiveFilters` already increments for non-default sort (from sub-task C) so the filter badge auto-reflects an active sort. Tests in new `__tests__/collection-detail-sort-gate.test.ts` (15 cases / 3 suites): **the corruption-fix structural pin** that the drag-mode branch's condition includes `itemFilters.sort === "default"` (with the explanatory comment block immediately after), `applySortMode` import alongside `applyItemFilters`, the pipeline ordering `applyItemFilters → applySortMode → useChunkedList` via `String.search` index comparison, sort-memo deps pinned to `[filteredItems, itemFilters.sort]` (NOT `[filteredItems, itemFilters]`), sort label rendered via `t("sortLabel")`, all 3 mode literals (`"default"`/`"name-asc"`/`"name-desc"`) present with `accessibilityRole="button"`, write-back uses `setDraft({ ...draft, sort: opt.mode })` (spread preserves other fields), all 5 sort styles declared (`sortRow`/`sortChip`/`sortChipActive`/`sortChipText`/`sortChipTextActive`), sort field placed below `filterHasPhotos` and above `sheetActions` (affordance ordering), all 4 sort i18n keys present in the `en` base table, each of the 4 keys localized in ru/be/pl/de/es, and an exact 6-declarations-per-key count (en + 5 overrides). [DONE: 2026-05-21] [est: 700] - Auto-tick the "Listed X ago" / chat preview timestamps every 60 seconds via a single shared `useNow()` hook so a chat preview that says "1 minute ago" rolls over to "2 minutes ago" without requiring a screen re-mount. A 30-line hook in `lib/use-now.ts` would close the gap. — New `lib/use-now.ts` exporting `useNow(intervalMs = 60_000): number` plus a pure `resolveInterval` clamp + a `USE_NOW_DEFAULT_TICK_MS` constant. The hook seeds state via `useState<number>(() => Date.now())` (lazy initializer — `useState(Date.now())` would re-evaluate `Date.now()` on every render; the function form runs the initializer exactly once), registers `setInterval(..., safeInterval)` inside `useEffect` with a `clearInterval` cleanup, and re-creates the interval when `intervalMs` changes by listing it in the dep array (so a parent passing a different cadence doesn't end up with two timers). `resolveInterval` clamps non-finite / non-positive overrides to the default — without it, `useNow(Infinity)` crashes setInterval, `useNow(NaN)` is undefined behaviour, and `useNow(0)` spins the event loop. 60s is the default tick because relative labels under an hour only change at minute boundaries — faster wastes CPU, slower lets the label visibly stale. **Deliberately NOT wiring it into the four consumers** (`app/chats.tsx`, `app/listing/[id].tsx`, `app/settings.tsx`) in this task — the call-site migrations are listed as follow-up suggestions; this task is the hook itself per its literal phrasing ("A 30-line hook in `lib/use-now.ts` would close the gap"). New `__tests__/use-now.test.ts` (9 cases / 2 suites): `resolveInterval` returns the input for positive finite values, falls back to default for `Infinity` / `NaN` / `0` / negative, and the default is 60_000 (pinned so a future "let's tick every 5s" mistake fails loudly); structural — useState+useEffect react imports, lazy `() => Date.now()` initializer (catches the eager-eval regression), setInterval+clearInterval cleanup, `resolveInterval(intervalMs)` threading into setInterval, and the `[intervalMs]` dep array (so changing the cadence re-creates the timer). - Track-and-document a `scripts/sentry-doctor.ts` self-check script that prints whether the DSN is reachable, whether sourcemaps for the latest deploy exist, and whether the most recent release was tagged. Wire it into a `npm run sentry:check` script so engineers can validate the wiring without poking the Sentry UI. Cheap to write — uses `fetch` against the Sentry public API.

- Promote the `@sentry/react-native` peer dep into the existing `lib/cloudinary-config.ts` env-validation pattern by adding a `scripts/check-required-env.ts` that fails CI when a `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` documented in `README-DEPLOY.md` is missing from `eas.json`'s implicit secret references. Avoids adding a new env var to one workflow and forgetting the other.

- Pre-load the Sentry RN SDK lazily via `import("@sentry/react-native")` only when `enabled === true`, so dev/test bundles never pay the ~120 KB native bridge cost. The Crash #2 / Crash #3 tasks already imply lazy import; codify it as a hard requirement in `lib/sentry.ts` with a structural test that fails on any top-level `import * as Sentry from "@sentry/react-native"` outside the lazy path.

- Add a `.env.example` despite it currently being gitignored — flip line 35 of `.gitignore` to track it and seed it with placeholder values for every `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` listed in `README-DEPLOY.md`. Today new engineers have to read README-DEPLOY.md to know what to set; a tracked `.env.example` is the canonical Expo / React Native onboarding pattern and pairs naturally with the existing `cloudinaryConfig` resolver tests.

Implement: the designs in this project

- Generate `docs/powerbi-connection.md`'s schema-reference table from `lib/analytics-events.ts` at build time (e.g. a `scripts/generate-powerbi-schema-doc.ts` step) so a new event added to the typed union shows up in the BI doc automatically. Today the property-key sub-table is hand-maintained; a future event that's emitted but undocumented becomes an "unknown column" in Power Query.

- Add a Power BI quick-start CLI under `scripts/print-powerbi-conn.ts` that reads the user's `.env` and prints the exact session-pooler connection string + service-role placeholder so engineers don't have to dig through the Supabase dashboard. Useful onboarding helper that pairs nicely with `docs/powerbi-connection.md` step 2.

- Document a free **Metabase** fallback path alongside the Power BI guide for Linux engineers who can't run Power BI Desktop. Same `analytics_events` table, same DAX-equivalent SQL queries; a `docs/metabase-connection.md` companion would close the platform-parity gap without us paying for cross-platform Power BI.

- Add a `docs/powerbi-cost-projection.md` companion that translates "free Power BI Desktop is fine for personal dashboards" into a concrete tipping point ("you'll need Power BI Pro at \$10/user/mo when you want scheduled refresh and >2 viewers"). Today the doc says "manual refresh is usually fine" but doesn't surface *when* to budget for the upgrade.

- Wire a CI-side query that runs the three DAX measures' SQL-equivalent against a tiny seeded `analytics_events` fixture and asserts the expected DAU / funnel / conversion-rate values. Today the DAX is documented but not validated; a one-off `__tests__/powerbi-dax-equivalents.test.ts` translating each measure into raw SQL would catch a typo in the documented formulas before someone wires them into a real dashboard.

- Replace the hand-rolled `timingSafeEqual` in `supabase/functions/analytics-mirror/index.ts` with Deno's `crypto.timingSafeEqual` once a TextEncoder helper is added. Today the JS-level XOR loop is correct but a primitive crypto call is shorter and avoids the per-character UTF-16 quirk on multi-byte secrets.

- Add a `payload-too-large` 413 response to `analytics-mirror` capped at, say, 256KB. Today PostHog could batch hundreds of events into one POST and we'd attempt the insert; bounding the body up front is cheaper than letting Postgres reject a huge insert and is more defensive against a misconfigured PostHog destination.

- Promote `extractEvents` from `analytics-mirror/index.ts` into `lib/analytics-mirror-payload.ts` so it's unit-tested alongside `buildAnalyticsEventRow`. Today the single-vs-batch detection is only smoke-tested via the structural function test; pulling it into the typed transformer would let us add Node tests for "batch with one item", "deeply nested non-batch", "null payload", etc.

- Add an `EXPO_PUBLIC_POSTHOG_WEBHOOK_TIMEOUT_MS` knob and respond 504 if the Supabase insert exceeds it. Today a slow/hung Postgres connection would tie up the Edge Function until the platform's hard timeout; a self-imposed 5s ceiling lets PostHog retry sooner with the standard exponential backoff.

- Capture a Sentry breadcrumb from the Edge Function on partial-success (`status === 207`) so a spike of `errors[]` entries surfaces in the crash dashboard. Today a malformed event is silently 207'd; cross-tagging into Sentry gives operations a single pane of glass instead of having to grep Edge Function logs.

- Promote the migration-structural-test pattern (introduced for `__tests__/analytics-events-migration.test.ts` and `chat-messages-migration.test.ts`) into a shared `__tests__/helpers/sql-migration-asserts.ts` exposing `assertColumns(source, columns)`, `assertIndex(source, name, on)`, `assertRlsEnabled(source, table)`, `assertNoPolicies(source, table)`, and `assertManualTasksDocuments(migrationFile)`. Today every migration test re-rolls the same regex shapes; centralising them would shrink the next migration test from ~120 to ~30 lines and force consistent shorthand.

- Add a `scripts/check-supabase-migration-naming.ts` lint step that asserts every file under `supabase/migrations/` matches `^\d{8}_[a-z0-9_]+\.sql$` AND has a matching entry in `MANUAL-TASKS.md`. Today the CLAUDE.md DB-change rule is enforced only by reviewer attention; a deterministic check would catch a forgotten manual-tasks entry the moment it lands in CI.

- Cross-check that every `analytics_events.name` value the app emits (i.e. the union in `lib/analytics-events.ts`) fits within the migration's `CHECK (length(name) <= 200)` cap. Today the cap is enforced server-side but the typed-union doesn't visibly assert its values stay short; a `__tests__/analytics-events-name-bounded.test.ts` that iterates `EVENT_NAMES` and asserts `length <= 200` makes the contract explicit.

- Add a `lib/analytics-mirror-payload.ts` typed builder that takes a PostHog payload and returns a row shaped like `{ user_id, name, properties, occurred_at }` matching the Analytics #12 schema, plus a `__tests__/analytics-mirror-payload.test.ts`. Today Analytics #13's Edge Function will inevitably hand-roll this mapping; pre-extracting it client-side gives a typed contract and a unit-tested transformer that the Edge Function can import.

- Add an `EXPO_PUBLIC_ANALYTICS_MIRROR_DISABLED` kill-switch read inside `lib/analytics-config.ts` that, when true, prevents the upcoming `analytics-mirror` webhook from being configured (Analytics #13). Useful for incident response (drop the long-tail event store without redeploying) and for offline-only QA where a user wants Posthog-only flow.

- Promote the `setupFakeDom()` helper from `__tests__/clarity.test.ts` into a shared `__tests__/helpers/fake-dom.ts` so future web-only modules (a hypothetical Plausible / GA4 wiring, OpenGraph meta-tag injection, service-worker registration tests) can reuse the same minimal `document` / `window` stub without each one re-inventing the parentNode / getElementById / createElement mocks. Today the fake DOM is co-located with one test file; a shared helper plus a 5-test regression suite would let every web-only module ship with parity coverage.

- Add a `lib/clarity.ts` `addClarityCustomTag(key, value)` wrapper exposing Microsoft Clarity's `clarity("set", key, value)` API so the analytics call sites can attach segmentation tags (e.g. `set("isPremium", "true")`, `set("language", "ru")`) to the active replay session. Today the queue stub is seeded but no helper exposes it — a 10-line wrapper that calls through `window.clarity?.("set", k, v)` after the gates pass would let `AnalyticsProvider` mirror the `identifyUser` traits into the Clarity replay timeline without each call site reaching into globals.

- Wire a `clarity-input-mask` audit step into `lint:ci` that greps `app/**/*.tsx` + `components/**/*.tsx` for `<TextInput` / raw `<input` and asserts each one carries the `data-clarity-mask` web-only prop (or sits inside a wrapper with `class="ms-clarity-mask"`). Today the docs declare "mask all `<input>`s" as a hard requirement but nothing enforces it — a single forgotten input on the email-OTP form would leak the address to Microsoft's replay bucket.

- Add a runtime warning in `lib/clarity.ts:initClarity` that `console.warn`s once when `analyticsConfig.clarityId` is set but `analyticsConfig.enabled === false` (i.e. dev-mode operator pasted the project ID into `.env` expecting it to load). Today the no-op is silent and the operator is left wondering why no replay rows appear in the Clarity dashboard; a one-time log keyed off a module-scoped `warned` flag closes the gap without polluting production.

- Capture a Sentry breadcrumb (`addBreadcrumb("clarity loaded", { clarityId, doNotTrack })`) the first time `initClarity()` succeeds so a future crash report includes whether the replay tag was active at the time. Today the two telemetry stacks are independent; cross-tagging the breadcrumb makes it possible to grep crashes by "did Clarity ever load?" — useful when debugging users who can't reproduce.

Today the function is duplicated; a future "preview" environment added to one would silently fall back to "production" in the other.
