- Track `listing_view` when a user opens `app/listing/[id].tsx` for someone else's listing, debounced so pagination scrolls don't spam events. Pairs naturally with `listing_claimed` to compute the view-to-buy conversion rate. Reuses the same debounce primitive that Analytics #10 (`chat_opened`) needs.

- Promote the inline 500ms `setTimeout`/`clearTimeout` debounce in `app/chat/[id].tsx` into a generic `useDwellTimeEffect(deps, ms, fire)` hook in `lib/use-dwell-time.ts` so future "user actually engaged with X for ≥ms" events (`listing_view`, `profile_view`, `collection_view`) reuse the same primitive. Today the pattern is hand-rolled per call site; centralising shrinks each future event to one line.

- Add a `friend_request_accepted` event paired with the new `friend_requested` so the social-graph funnel has both arms. Today `addFriend` fires only the outgoing send; mutual acceptance (when `incoming && outgoing` flips to `friend`) is invisible. Trigger from the same `useEffect` that derives `friends` in social-context, gated on the previous-vs-next `friends` set diff.

- Mirror the `alreadyRequested` dedup in `removeFriend` with a `friend_request_cancelled` event so churn metrics show outgoing requests that didn't convert. Today removing a request is invisible; pairing it with the send event enables a complete funnel (sent → accepted | cancelled | expired).

- Capture the `premium_activated.source` from the actual screen that triggered the upgrade (settings vs paywall vs listing-cap-CTA) by threading a single `lastPremiumIntent` ref through `usePremium()`. Today the bottom-nav source is hardcoded to `"settings"`; surfacing the real origin lets Power BI rank which surface drives the most upgrades.

- Add a structural test that asserts every `trackEvent("X")` call across `app/**` and `lib/**` matches a key in `ANALYTICS_EVENTS` — the AST-based regex test in `analytics-events.test.ts` only verifies the union; this guards against a future call site passing a literal string that isn't typed (e.g. via `as AnalyticsEventName` cast).

## Tasks promoted from .suggestions.md (2026-05-25)


### Geometry tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Migrate `borderRadius: 999` (71 inline occurrences) to `RADIUS_PILL` across `app/` and `components/`** — the most-recurring inline value in the codebase; pill chips, badges, and round buttons all share it. A single `npm run lint:radius` companion to the new `lint:hex` guard (same scanner shape) would catch regressions once the migration lands. The 71 occurrences span ~25 files — bite-sized per-file migration sub-tasks would mirror the design-tokens hex migration pattern.

- **Migrate `borderRadius: 22` (48 occurrences) to `RADIUS_CARD` and `borderRadius: 24` (25 occurrences) to `RADIUS_CARD_LG`** — these are the two card-surface anchors; both are intentional design rhythms (cards 22, sheet wrappers 24) so co-locating the values lets a designer flip the entire card family in one edit. Pair with the existing token-adoption test pattern that already covers each migrated file.

- **Migrate `gap: 10` (57 occurrences) to `SPACING_LIST`, `gap: 12` (43) to `SPACING_CARD`, and `gap: 8` (38) to `SPACING_INLINE`** — these are the three most-recurring gap values; together they cover 138 occurrences (66% of all `gap:` declarations). Per-file migration sub-tasks aligned with the geometry-token names would close the consistency gap with minimal review burden.

- **Extend the inline-hex scanner to also flag `borderRadius: <literal>` and `gap: <literal>`** — today `lint:hex` only catches color literals. A `lint:geometry` step that fails on inline `borderRadius: 22`/`gap: 10` (etc.) inside `app/`+`components/` would enforce the new geometry-token convention the same way the hex check enforces the palette convention. The same pure-helper + script-wrapper + test-trio pattern applies.

- **Add a `lib/styles.ts` aggregator that re-exports both the palette and the geometry tokens under a single `tokens` namespace** — today consumers import named values one at a time, which means every file has a ~10-line import block. A `import { tokens } from "@/lib/styles"` aggregator + `backgroundColor: tokens.CARD_BG, borderRadius: tokens.RADIUS_CARD` would shave 5-15 LOC per file. Pairs naturally with the proposed `tokens preview` route.

### Inline-hex CI guardrail (2026-05-25)

- **Extend the scan to `.ts` files (not just `.tsx`)** — today only `.tsx` is walked, but `lib/placeholder-color.ts` and any future utility module could legitimately compute or hard-code a color value. Widening the scanner to `.ts` would need a corresponding allowlist for the few utilities that intentionally produce hex strings (`lib/placeholder-color.ts` derives one from an item id) — either by checking exact file paths or by allowing hex literals inside template/computation contexts like `\`#\${hue.toString(16)}\``. A 20-line addition.

- **Add a 3-digit shorthand check (`#fff`/`#abc`) once the `OVERLAY_*` family lands** — the migration deliberately preserved 3-digit `#fff` in 8 files (chats, friends, wishlist, settings, create, item, collection, item-card) because pure-white badge text is genuinely intentional. Once we add `PURE_WHITE` adoption testing across those callers (or wrap them in `<Text style={[..., {color: PURE_WHITE}]}>`), extend the scanner's regex to `#[0-9a-fA-F]{3,6}` to close the last hex backdoor. Same applies to the `rgba(...)` literals — once `OVERLAY_*` lands, they should join the deny list.

- **Catch `from` / `via` / `to` gradient stops with hex values inside `<LinearGradient>`** — today the migration is StyleSheet-focused, but JSX literals like `colors={["#abc...", "#def..."]}` would slip through if a contributor passes them inline. The current scanner DOES catch JSX-string-literal hex (it's just a 6-digit regex), but the test coverage doesn't pin a JSX-specific case. Adding one would future-proof against a `<LinearGradient colors={["#001122", "#334455"]}>` regression.

- **Report findings inline as GitHub PR annotations via `::error file=...,line=...,col=...::`** — the script currently `process.exit(1)`s with a console-formatted report, which shows up in the CI logs but not as line-level review comments. The GitHub Actions log-command format would surface each finding as a click-through annotation on the PR diff. ~10 lines around the `console.error` call.

- **Promote the scanner into a reusable `lib/lint-*.ts` family + `scripts/lint-*.ts` aggregator** — the same shape (pure helper + script wrapper + test) applies to other code-style guards we've discussed: no-circular-imports, no-`process.env[varName]`-foot-gun, no-emoji-in-translation-keys. A `scripts/lint-all.ts` that fans out to each guard and reports the aggregate would simplify the CI workflow YAML to a single step.

### ItemCard design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Migrate the `tagBadgeText: color: "#fff"` 3-digit shorthand to `PURE_WHITE`** — the migration deliberately preserved the `#fff` literal because the 6-digit regex doesn't catch it, but the inline shorthand is the last hex literal in the file. Routing it through `PURE_WHITE` would unify the convention even though the regex passes today, and it gives the future ESLint guardrail (already queued in `.tasks.md`) a uniform target to grep against rather than having to maintain a separate 3-digit allowlist.

- **Wrap `ItemCard` in `React.memo` like `SelectableItemRow` (VM-F)** — `ItemCard` is the only un-memoized row component in the chunked-list / FlatList stack on `app/collection/[id].tsx`. The masonry FlatList passes `renderItem={({item}) => <View ...><ItemCard item={item} compact /></View>}` which allocates a fresh wrapper each render; combined with the unmemoized `ItemCard` itself this is the second-largest re-render cost in the screen (after the just-fixed selectable row). The VM-F recipe applies directly: `React.memo(function ItemCard(...))` + hoist the wrapper JSX into a `useCallback` renderItem on the FlatList caller.

- **Lazy-load `<Image>` photos via a `priority="low"` `onLoadStart` / `onLoadEnd` skeleton** — today every `ItemCard` with a photo immediately fires a `withCloudinaryThumbUrl` request on mount. With chunked pagination capping the mount count at 20, the page-1 load is fine — but page 2+ would benefit from an `expo-image` migration (or a manual `priority` shim on the existing `Image`) that defers offscreen photos. The skeleton placeholder using the new `AMBER_MUTED_3` background already gives the right visual fallback.

- **Co-locate `placeholderColor(item.id)` with the rest of the design tokens** — today the function lives in `lib/placeholder-color.ts` and computes a deterministic warm-brown hue per item id, but the function isn't part of the central palette. Wiring it into `lib/design-tokens.ts` as `placeholderColorForId(id)` would let the future `tokens preview` route (already in suggestions) demonstrate the function alongside the static tokens, and would make the deterministic-color pattern discoverable for future "deterministic avatar" code.

- **Extract the `cost: number | null` + `costCurrency: string | null` rendering into a `<CostBadge>` component** — the same `{t("costLabel")}: {item.cost}{item.costCurrency ? ` ${item.costCurrency}` : ""}` pattern appears in both `card` (line 78) and `compactCard` (line 31) branches of `ItemCard`, AND in `app/item/[id].tsx`'s detail view, AND in the `app/collection/[id].tsx` total-cost summary. A single `<CostBadge amount={item.cost} currency={item.costCurrency} />` component would centralise the formatting logic — pairs naturally with the `formatCostAmount` helper shipped in the currency-conversion task.

### CurrencyInput design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Co-locate `CURRENCY_CHIPS` with a `getCurrencySymbol(code)` helper in `lib/locale-helpers.ts`** — today `<CurrencyInput>` renders the raw 3-letter currency code (`USD`/`EUR`/`RUB`) as the leading "symbol" inside `currencySymbol` styled text, but the visual cue would be much stronger if it rendered `$` / `€` / `₽` instead. The `Intl.NumberFormat` API can derive the symbol via `(new Intl.NumberFormat("en", { style: "currency", currency: code }).formatToParts(0).find(p => p.type === "currency").value)` — a 10-line helper would replace the all-caps code with the proper glyph (falling back to the code for currencies without a Unicode symbol). Pairs naturally with the `LANGUAGE_CURRENCY` env-override work already shipped.

- **Render `parseCurrencyValue` errors inline with a `MUTED_27` muted-error pill instead of silently returning `null`** — today the form swallows invalid inputs (non-finite, ≤0, empty) and the caller has no signal to surface "please enter a positive amount". A `parseCurrencyValue` upgrade returning `{value: number, error: null} | {value: null, error: "empty" | "non-positive"}` plus a small error-pill component (DANGER_SOFT bg + DANGER_DEEP_2 text) would close the UX gap without changing the happy path's shape.

- **Add a "currency picker sheet" alternative to the horizontal chip strip for users with 5+ pinned currencies** — today `CURRENCY_CHIPS` exposes 10 currencies as a `ScrollView`-driven row, but on a small viewport (iPhone SE) the user has to scroll to see PLN/UAH/JPY/CNY. A bottom-sheet picker (mirroring the `<CurrencySheet>` already used in `app/collection/[id].tsx`) triggered by a "+" chip would let power users pin the 4 they care about and dig into the full 150-entry `CURRENCIES` list via the existing sheet when needed.

- **Type the `currency` and `onChangeCurrency` props as `CurrencyChipCode | (string & {})`** — today both are loose `string`s, but the `CURRENCY_CHIPS as const` already exposes the literal union via `CurrencyChipCode` (shipped in the `LANGUAGE_CURRENCY` migration). The `(string & {})` trick keeps the prop assignable to any string (so the sheet picker upstream can still pass arbitrary 3-letter codes) while surfacing the 10 chip currencies in IntelliSense — same upgrade pattern already logged for `EmptyState` props.

- **Migrate the `sanitize()` helper into `lib/format-cost.ts` (or a new `lib/format-currency-input.ts`)** — today it lives as a private function inside `components/currency-input.tsx`, but the comma-to-dot normalization + decimal-digit gate is a pure-string transformation that any future form field accepting amounts (refund inputs, price-suggestion sheets, marketplace listing forms) will need. Extracting it lets `__tests__/format-cost.test.ts` pick up regression coverage for the input-side parsing path the same way it already covers output-side formatting.

### EmptyState design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Audit the rest of the codebase for stray `EmptyState` usages that pass color overrides** — the new token-driven `wrap` / `iconOuter` / `iconMiddle` / `iconInner` styles inherit through props today, but if a caller ever overrides `backgroundColor` via a wrapper `<View>` the cream-on-cream layered visual would silently break. A `grep components/empty-state -A 3` sweep across `app/`+`components/` to confirm no caller wraps `<EmptyState>` in a custom-colored container would close the regression vector.

- **Promote the 3-tier `iconOuter` → `iconMiddle` → `iconInner` concentric-circle pattern into a reusable `<IconBadge>` component** — the same three nested `<View>` rings appear nowhere else today, but the visual is striking enough to be a candidate for premium upsell prompts, onboarding screens, and the future "achievement unlocked" badge. Extracting it would also let designers tune the cream-to-amber gradient (CARD_BG_2 → CARD_BG_3 → CARD_BG_14) by editing one component instead of three nested style entries.

- **Add a `tone: "neutral" | "premium" | "danger"` prop to `EmptyState` that swaps the AMBER_SOFT_3 dashed border + AMBER_ACCENT action bg for `MUTED_4` / `AMBER_ACCENT` / `DANGER_DEEP_2` variants respectively** — today every empty state renders with the same warm amber treatment, but premium-locked surfaces could benefit from a richer gradient and destructive flows (e.g. "all items deleted") could surface a soft-red surface. The token plumbing is already in place; this is purely a prop-driven style switch.

- **Migrate the `borderStyle: "dashed"` rendering test** — React Native Web renders dashed borders inconsistently across browsers (Safari + Firefox honor it; Chrome on Android sometimes drops it). A visual regression test using a headless browser screenshot would catch silent drops, especially since `EmptyState` is the only component in the design-tokens-migrated set that uses `borderStyle: "dashed"`. Without it, a future React Native Web upgrade could mute the visual without anyone noticing.

- **Co-locate the `iconOuter`/`iconMiddle`/`iconInner` ring sizes (96/76/56) into `lib/design-tokens.ts` as `RING_OUTER_SIZE = 96` / `RING_MIDDLE_SIZE = 76` / `RING_INNER_SIZE = 56` constants** — today the magic numbers live inline in the StyleSheet; promoting them follows the same pattern as the suggested `RADIUS_*` / `SPACING_*` tokens (already in `.tasks.md`). The concentric ratio (96 → 76 → 56 = 20px step) is intentional and worth pinning so a future tweak doesn't shuffle the visual rhythm. Pairs naturally with the proposed `<IconBadge>` extraction above.

### SelectableItemRow memo VM-F (2026-05-24)

- **Add `getItemLayout` to the selection-mode FlatList now that VM-F's memoization is in place** — `<SelectableItemRow>` is a fixed-height row (single-line title + 44px checkbox, no variable content), so handing `getItemLayout={(_, index) => ({ length: ROW_HEIGHT, offset: ROW_HEIGHT * index, index })}` to FlatList lets the recycler skip the `onLayout` measurement pass entirely. Even with `scrollEnabled={false}` (outer ScrollView owns scroll), the windowing math runs faster when row geometry is known up-front — pairs naturally with the just-shipped `renderSelectableRow` useCallback + extraData wiring. Same trick the viewer FlatList can also pick up.

- **Promote `toggleSelect`'s `useCallback` pattern across the rest of `app/collection/[id].tsx`'s handler stack** — VM-F converted `toggleSelect` from a plain function to a `useCallback` with empty deps because the row memo needed a stable `onToggle` ref. The same shape applies to `enterSelectionMode`, `exitSelectionMode`, `performBulkDelete`, `handleOpenMove`, and `handleBulkDelete` — they're all currently re-allocated every render but are passed into memoized children (bulk-bar buttons, header chrome). One bulk-edit pass closes the consistency gap before more memoized children land.

- **Replace `selectedIds.has(item.id)` lookups with a per-row `selected` boolean derived once per render** — today the row's `selected` prop is computed inline in `renderSelectableRow` (`selected={selectedIds.has(item.id)}`), which means every visible row pays a Set hash lookup per parent render. For collections with thousands of items in the chunked window, hoisting the lookup into a `selectedById = useMemo(() => Object.fromEntries(Array.from(selectedIds).map(id => [id, true])), [selectedIds])` map and reading `selected={!!selectedById[item.id]}` is a measurable win — same complexity, half the constant factor because the V8 hidden-class lookup is cheaper than `Set.prototype.has`'s generic dispatch. Marginal but free.

- **Add a `__DEV__`-only `React.profiler` wrapper around the selection-mode FlatList to validate that VM-F actually reduces re-renders in practice** — VM-F's structural tests pin the shape but don't measure the actual perf win. A 10-LOC dev-only Profiler that logs `actualDuration` per row commit (gated on `__DEV__ && selectedIds.size > 0`) would surface in the Metro logs the moment a future refactor accidentally re-introduces the unmemoized renderItem. Strip from prod via the `__DEV__` guard.

- **Pin a structural test that `components/selectable-item-row.tsx` exports a `memo(...)` wrapper AND that the inner function is named `SelectableItemRow`** — VM-F's test asserts the memo wrapper but doesn't check the named-function form (`memo(function SelectableItemRow(...))` rather than `memo((props) => ...)`). The named form gives React DevTools a real component name in the profiler tree — without it, the row shows up as "Anonymous" and is much harder to diagnose. A 1-line `assert.match(src, /memo\(function\s+SelectableItemRow\b/)` closes the gap.

### Selection-mode FlatList VM-E (2026-05-24)

- **Add `getItemLayout` to the selection-mode FlatList** — `<SelectableItemRow>` is a fixed-height row (single-line title + 44px checkbox, no variable content), so handing `getItemLayout={(_, index) => ({ length: ROW_HEIGHT, offset: ROW_HEIGHT * index, index })}` to FlatList lets the recycler skip the `onLayout` measurement pass entirely. Even with `scrollEnabled={false}` (outer ScrollView owns scroll), the windowing math runs faster when row geometry is known up-front — same trick the viewer FlatList can also pick up (see VM-D suggestions).

- **Memoize the selection-mode `renderItem` via `useCallback`** — today the inline arrow `({ item }) => (<SelectableItemRow item={item} selected={selectedIds.has(item.id)} onToggle={toggleSelect} />)` allocates a fresh closure every render, so React.memo on `<SelectableItemRow>` sees a new function reference each pass and can't actually skip work. Promoting to `const renderSelectableRow = useCallback(({ item }) => ..., [selectedIds, toggleSelect])` unlocks skip-work for rows whose selected state didn't change. Pair with `extraData={selectedIds}` so FlatList knows to re-render when the selection set changes despite the data array being stable.

- **Wrap `<SelectableItemRow>` in `React.memo` if it isn't already** — VM-E's renderItem indirection is only valuable if `<SelectableItemRow>` actually skips re-render when its props are referentially stable. A quick audit of `components/selectable-item-row.tsx` plus a `React.memo` wrapper (if missing) closes the loop — same shape as the existing `ItemCard` memoization VM-A/B/C/D builds on.

- **Move the bulk-bar out of the FlatList's render tree so selection mode can own its own scroll** — today the bulk-bar is pinned absolute to the viewport which is why VM-E kept `scrollEnabled={false}`. But the absolute-positioning + nested ScrollView creates an iOS-specific touch-handling edge case (taps near the bulk-bar can fall through to the underlying ScrollView). Hoisting the bulk-bar OUT of the FlatList's children entirely (it's already a sibling at the JSX level, but the outer `<Screen nestable>` still owns scroll), then flipping the FlatList to `scrollEnabled={true}` with a VM-D-style `<Screen scroll={false}>` wrapping pattern, would let selection mode also unlock iOS row recycling.

- **Replace the chunked-window `useChunkedList(items)` Load-more CTA with FlatList's native `onEndReached` pagination** — today selection-mode + viewer both use `useChunkedList` (manual "Load more" CTA). With FlatList now owning the renderItem path in BOTH modes (selection via VM-E, viewer via VM-D), the manual chunked window is redundant. `onEndReached={loadMore}` + `onEndReachedThreshold={0.5}` would auto-extend the window as the user scrolls, removing the explicit Load-more button entirely. Backward-compatible: the existing `loadMore` callback already handles the extension; only the trigger changes.

### FlatList viewer migration VM-D (2026-05-24)

- **Add `getItemLayout` to the viewer FlatList** — VM-D enabled `windowSize={5}` + `initialNumToRender={10}` but FlatList still pays an `onLayout` measurement on every row before it can decide what to recycle. `<ItemCard compact />` is fixed-height (110px image + ~70px text padding ≈ 180px row), so `getItemLayout={(_, index) => ({ length: 180, offset: 180 * Math.floor(index / 2), index })}` (divide by `numColumns` for grid math) hands the geometry to FlatList up-front. Measurable scroll-perf win on long collections — the recycler can skip directly to the right offset instead of measuring sequentially.

- **Hoist the viewer FlatList `renderItem` into a memoized `useCallback`** — today the early-return contains an inline `({ item }) => (<View style={styles.masonryItem}><ItemCard item={item} compact /></View>)` arrow that's reallocated on every render. React.memo on `<ItemCard>` (which exists internally) sees a fresh function reference each pass and can't actually skip work. Promoting to `const renderViewerItem = useCallback(({ item }) => ..., [])` (no closed-over props except the static styles) re-establishes memoization for free. Pairs with the existing `keyExtractor={(item) => item.id}` pattern.

- **Pin a regression test that the viewer-FlatList path does NOT pass `data={items}` (only `data={visibleItems}`)** — VM-A/B/C/D all bound the mount count via the chunked-list window; a future contributor swapping `data={visibleItems}` → `data={items}` would silently re-introduce the unbounded mount that the entire VM series was designed to prevent. The current `__tests__/collection-detail-vm-d-viewer-scroll.test.ts` asserts a positive `data={visibleItems}` shape but doesn't have a `doesNotMatch(/data=\{\s*items\s*\}/)` companion — adding one closes the only obvious regression vector.

- **Extract the new `pageHeader` / `listTitleAndFilters` / `loadMoreCta` / `modalsBlock` consts into stable `useMemo`'d React nodes** — today they're declared as inline const fragments inside the render function so they allocate fresh JSX trees on every parent re-render. `useMemo(() => (<View ...>...</View>), [activeCollection.id, allItems.length, ...])` would let the FlatList's `ListHeaderComponent` see a stable reference and avoid re-mounting the header on every scroll-driven re-render (a real perf win because the hero `<Image>` mounts a Cloudinary fetch).

- **Migrate `app/wishlist.tsx` and `app/collections-feed.tsx` to the same `<Screen scroll={false}>` + `<FlatList>` pattern that VM-D shipped here** — both screens currently render long item / collection lists inside the existing nestable ScrollView pattern, so they have the same unbounded-mount issue VM-A/B/C/D fixed for collection detail. Same diff shape: ListHeaderComponent for chrome, ListFooterComponent for any "load more" CTA, and the new `viewerFlatList` + `viewerFlatListContent` styles can be lifted into `lib/design-tokens.ts` (or a shared `styles/flat-list.ts`) so this becomes a one-line import per screen instead of a copy.

### FlatList viewer migration VM-C (2026-05-24)

- **Add `getItemLayout` to the viewer FlatList so virtualization can skip layout measurement** — today the FlatList has no `getItemLayout` prop, so even after VM-D unlocks true windowing, every row pays an `onLayout` measurement before windowing decisions are made. Compact `ItemCard` is fixed-height (110px image + ~70px text padding = ~180px row), so `getItemLayout={(_, index) => ({ length: 180, offset: 180 * Math.floor(index / 2), index })}` (divide by `numColumns` for grid math) gives FlatList the row geometry up front and removes the measurement cost — measurable scroll-perf win on long collections.

- **Set `removeClippedSubviews={Platform.OS === "ios"}` on the viewer FlatList immediately (don't wait for VM-D)** — even with `scrollEnabled={false}` while nested inside the outer ScrollView, `removeClippedSubviews` still lets the JS thread skip rendering off-screen cells when the OUTER scroll moves them out of the visible viewport. iOS Safari WebView in particular benefits. One-line change today, zero risk, defers the harder VM-D refactor.

- **Pin a structural test that the viewer FlatList does NOT carry `data={items}` (only `data={visibleItems}`)** — today's VM-C tests assert `data={visibleItems}` is present but a future contributor swapping to `data={items}` would re-introduce the unbounded mount that VM-A/B fixed. A `assert.doesNotMatch(src, /<FlatList[\s\S]*?data=\{\s*items\s*\}/)` (combined with the existing positive assertion) closes the regression vector — same shape as the "no inline modulo" guard from VM-B.

- **Extract the viewer FlatList renderItem into a memoized top-level `renderViewerItem` function** — today it's an inline `({ item }) => <View><ItemCard /></View>` arrow allocated on every render, so React.memo on `<ItemCard>` (already in place via the card's structure) sees a fresh closure each pass and can't actually skip work. Hoisting to `const renderViewerItem = useCallback(({ item }) => ..., [])` (or out of the component if it doesn't close over props) closes the memoization gap and pairs with the existing `keyExtractor={(item) => item.id}` pattern.

- **Replace the per-item `<View style={styles.masonryItem}>` wrapper with `style={styles.masonryItem}` directly on `<ItemCard>`** — today the wrapper exists purely to give each cell `flex: 1` so the two columns divide the row evenly. If `ItemCard` accepted a `style` prop and forwarded it to its outer `Pressable`/`View`, the wrapper layer would disappear (one less node per cell × hundreds of cells = measurable RN bridge / Yoga layout savings on long collections). Touches `ItemCard`'s prop signature (additive — no behavior change) and removes the wrapper in this caller.

### Masonry helper VM-B (2026-05-24)

- **Memoize `masonryColumns` via a `useMemo` on `[visibleItems, columnCount]` and accept `columnCount` from `useResponsive()` to render 3 cols on tablet / 4 on desktop** — today the column count is the literal `2` inside the `useMemo`, which is fine for mobile but wastes screen space on wide layouts. The helper already supports N columns (VM-A); the caller just hard-codes 2. A `const { isTablet, isDesktop } = useResponsive(); const cols = isDesktop ? 4 : isTablet ? 3 : 2;` one-liner before the memo would adapt without new helpers — but the JSX still hard-codes `masonryColumns[0]` / `masonryColumns[1]` so a parallel refactor mapping `masonryColumns.map((col, i) => <View key={i} style={i === 0 ? styles.masonryCol : [styles.masonryCol, styles.masonryColOffset]}>...)` is needed alongside.

- **Pin a unit test that the `useMemo` dep array on `masonryColumns` does NOT include `items` or `allItems`** — today the memo depends only on `visibleItems`, which is correct (the chunked-list window already narrows by `items` upstream). A future refactor that accidentally adds `items` to the dep array would re-allocate the columns on every chunked-list re-render even when the visible slice didn't actually change, defeating the memoization. A regex assertion on the exact dep contents (`\[\s*visibleItems\s*\]` — nothing else) would close the regression vector.

- **Extract the masonry render into a reusable `<MasonryGrid items={...} renderItem={...} columnCount={2} />` component** — the `<View masonryGrid> <View masonryCol> {col0.map(...)} </View> <View masonryCol masonryColOffset> {col1.map(...)} </View> </View>` markup is screen-specific today but the same shape will land on profile / collections-feed once those pick up the helper. A 30-LOC component co-located with `lib/masonry.ts` (or a sibling `components/masonry-grid.tsx`) would close the duplication class before the second consumer lands.

- **Replace the literal numeric index `masonryColumns[0]` / `masonryColumns[1]` access with a `.map((column, idx) => <View key={idx}>...)` so the JSX is column-count-agnostic** — pairs with the responsive `columnCount` upgrade above. Today the literal indices lock the layout at 2 columns even though the helper is N-column ready; mapping over the helper output decouples the JSX from the column count and makes the 3/4-column upgrade a one-line `cols = X` change.

- **Pin a structural test that `app/collection/[id].tsx` no longer carries any `\.filter\(\(_, i\) => i % 2` shape in the file** — VM-B's regression guard asserts the absence of `i % 2 === 0` and `i % 2 === 1` literals, but a future contributor could subtly re-introduce the pattern with `i % 2 !== 0` or `i % 2 < 1`. A broader regex (`i\s*%\s*2`) would catch every modulo-by-2 reintroduction, not just the specific literals that exist today.

### Masonry helper VM-A (2026-05-24)

- **Promote `distributeIntoMasonryColumns` to handle balanced-height masonry (not just round-robin)** — today the helper distributes by index modulo, which is fine when every `ItemCard` has the same rendered height. Once compact cards start carrying variable-height extras (price tag, condition pill, thumbnail aspect ratio), a card that's taller than its sibling drags column 0 below column 1 visually, breaking the staggered-flow illusion. A `distributeByHeight<T>(items, columnCount, getHeight: (item: T) => number): T[][]` variant that picks the shortest column at each step (greedy bin-packing) would close the visual gap with ~15 LOC and the same identity-preserving contract.

- **Wire `distributeIntoMasonryColumns` into a `useMasonryColumns(items, columnCount)` hook that memoizes the result via `useMemo`** — today VM-B would call the helper directly inside the JSX, which is fine for one screen but doesn't memoize across re-renders. A hook variant (mirroring `useChunkedList`'s API shape) would close the memoization gap before a second screen (e.g. profile masonry, collections feed) picks up the same helper and re-implements the same `useMemo(() => distributeIntoMasonryColumns(items, 2), [items])` boilerplate.

- **Add a `columnCount` responsiveness via `useResponsive()` so wide screens (tablet/desktop) render 3 or 4 columns instead of fixed 2** — the helper already supports N columns; the caller just hard-codes 2. A `const { isTablet, isDesktop } = useResponsive(); const cols = isDesktop ? 4 : isTablet ? 3 : 2;` one-liner before the `distributeIntoMasonryColumns(items, cols)` call would adapt the layout to the existing breakpoints (already used by `Screen` for `contentMaxWidth`). No new tokens needed — pure layout.

- **Pin a structural test in `__tests__/masonry-callers.test.ts` that asserts every call site uses `distributeIntoMasonryColumns` and not an inline `i % N` modulo** — today VM-B will migrate the one known call site, but nothing prevents a future contributor from re-introducing the `.filter((_, i) => i % 2 === N)` shape elsewhere. A repo-wide `grep` regression test (mirroring the design-tokens hex-literal gate) would fail loudly if the inline shape comes back in `app/**/*.tsx` or `components/**/*.tsx`.

- **Promote the empty-array allocation `Array.from({ length: safeCount }, () => [])` into a reusable `allocateColumns<T>(columnCount: number): T[][]` helper** — today it's a one-liner inside `distributeIntoMasonryColumns`, but the same shape will be needed by `distributeByHeight` (above) and any other column-aware helper. Exporting it would close the duplication class before the second consumer lands and give us a single place to add the `Object.freeze` defense if column-array mutation becomes a contract risk.

### Item-detail design-tokens migration (2026-05-23)

- **Pay off the `AMBER_MUTED_7` token in `app/collection/[id].tsx` (3 inline `#c4a87a` borderColor sites) and `SUCCESS_GREEN_2` in `app/collection/[id].tsx` (2 sites) + `components/visibility-badge.tsx` (2 sites) in the next migration pass** — both tokens were added during the item-detail migration specifically to close those upcoming gaps. Skipping them in the next pass means re-introducing the same inline literal that the central token was meant to eliminate, defeating the whole rotation-payoff narrative. A 4-LOC import-and-replace per file with the existing adoption-test pattern is enough.

- **Extract the `shareSheet` markup (handle bar + title/hint + link box + copy/native/cancel actions) into a reusable `<ShareSheet>` component** — today `app/item/[id].tsx` is the sole owner of the deep-link share flow but the same shape will land on `app/collection/[id].tsx` (collection deep-links already exist) and `app/profile/[id].tsx` (profile share). Three ~150 LOC duplications waiting to happen. The component would take `{ url, onClose, onCopy }` props and own its own styles + i18n keys.

- **Add a `useShareLink(deepLink)` hook that wraps `Share.share()` + `Clipboard.setStringAsync()` + the `copied` state + a 2-second reset timer** — today every share sheet that ships will re-implement the same `const [copied, setCopied] = useState(false)` + `setTimeout(() => setCopied(false), 2000)` ceremony alongside its own `Share.share` invocation. A 30 LOC hook plus a paired unit test closes the duplication class before the second consumer lands.

- **Pin a structural test that the migrated `app/item/[id].tsx` keeps its 5 deliberate `"#fff"` 3-digit literals (not 4, not 6)** — the migration sweep currently uses a 6-digit `#[0-9a-fA-F]{6}` regex to assert "no inline hex" but doesn't pin the 3-digit count. A future contributor refactoring `tagBadgeText` could collapse `color: "#fff"` to `color: PURE_WHITE` (a fine call) without realising the lint gate has been silently relaxed elsewhere. A `(src.match(/#[0-9a-fA-F]{3}\b/g) ?? []).length === 5` assertion would lock the intentional-preservation count.

- **Promote the `TAG_COLORS = [AMBER_ACCENT, TAG_RUST, TAG_SAGE, TAG_BLUE, TAG_PURPLE, TAG_TERRACOTTA, TAG_CYAN, TAG_GOLD, TAG_BROWN, TAG_TEAL]` 10-entry rotation array to `lib/design-tokens.ts`** — today the array is duplicated character-for-character between `app/create.tsx` and `app/item/[id].tsx`. If a future task tweaks the rotation (adds an 11th hue, re-orders the slots so brand-accent isn't first), only one file gets the update and the new-item form vs. the item-edit form drift visually. A `export const TAG_COLORS = [...] as const` next to the individual `TAG_*` exports plus a one-line import in both consumers closes the drift class with zero behaviour change.

### Sort UI + drag-mode gate (2026-05-23)

- **Surface a small banner/hint inside the masonry fallback when an owner has activated a non-default sort** — today owners silently lose drag-mode when picking A→Z/Z→A (the gate falls through to the read-only masonry). A one-line "Drag mode is off while sorting alphabetically — reset sort to reorder items" `<Text>` rendered above the masonry grid (gated on `isOwner && itemFilters.sort !== "default"`) would close the discoverability gap and prevent confusion ("why can't I drag rows anymore?"). Pairs naturally with a "Reset sort" inline pressable that calls `setItemFilters({ ...itemFilters, sort: "default" })`.

- **Pin the sort chip rendering via `accessibilityState={{ selected: active }}` on each `<Pressable>`** — the current implementation only carries `accessibilityRole="button"` so VoiceOver announces all 3 chips identically ("button") without indicating which is selected. The standard React Native pattern (`accessibilityState={{ selected }}`) makes VoiceOver read "selected" alongside the chip label — a 5-LOC change across the 3-chip render that closes the a11y gap.

- **Promote the 3-mode sort chip array (`[{ mode: "default", … }, { mode: "name-asc", … }, …]`) to a module-scoped `SORT_OPTIONS` constant in `lib/item-filters.ts`** — today the array is built inline inside the JSX of `<ItemFilterBar>`, so any future screen that wants the same picker (e.g. a global "Sort all collections" sheet) would re-implement the same 3-entry array. A 5-line export + paired structural test would eliminate the drift class and make the available sort modes a single source of truth.

- **Add a structural test pinning that `app/collection/[id].tsx` carries a comment explaining the drag-corruption gate** — the safety-critical condition `isOwner && !selectionMode && itemFilters.sort === "default"` looks like a stylistic choice without context. A `__tests__/collection-detail-sort-gate-comment.test.ts` grepping for "drag-corruption" or "silently re-write `sortOrder`" in the source ensures a future contributor refactoring the conditional understands WHY the sort gate exists and doesn't strip it as "dead code".

- **Surface the active sort mode as a removable quick-chip in the `<ItemFilterBar>` horizontal scroll** — today the active sort is invisible until the sheet is reopened (the `countActiveFilters` badge increments but doesn't name the active sort). A "↑ A→Z ✕" chip in the same `quickChips` row as the "With photos only" chip would give one-tap clear without the modal round-trip and let users see the active sort at a glance. Tap-to-clear writes `setItemFilters({ ...itemFilters, sort: "default" })` and the chip re-hides.

### In-collection sort logic (2026-05-23)

- **Cache the `Intl.Collator` instance behind `applySortMode` the same way `formatRelativeDate` caches `Intl.RelativeTimeFormat`** — today every call to `applySortMode(items, "name-asc")` walks ICU collation tables on each `a.title.localeCompare(b.title, undefined, { sensitivity: "base", numeric: true })` invocation (i.e. once per pair-compare during the `Array.prototype.sort` traversal — O(n log n) calls for an n-item collection). Hoisting a module-scoped `new Intl.Collator(undefined, { sensitivity: "base", numeric: true })` and routing through `collator.compare` would halve the per-sort CPU cost on collections with thousands of items. Mirror the `relativeTimeFormatCache` shape from `lib/i18n-context.tsx`.

- **Thread the user's current locale through `applySortMode(items, sort, locale)` so the comparator uses BCP-47 rules instead of `undefined`** — `localeCompare(_, undefined, …)` falls back to the JS runtime's default locale, which on iOS/Android is the device locale, but on a server-rendered web preview is whatever `Intl.DateTimeFormat().resolvedOptions().locale` returns (often `en-US`). For a Russian user who pinned the app language to `pl`, a German collator would silently disagree with what they see in the UI. A 1-line addition that grabs `useI18n().language` at the call site and passes it through closes the gap.

- **Add a `sortBy: "title" | "price" | "acquiredAt"` axis alongside `name-asc/name-desc`** — the current sort axis is hard-coded to `item.title`. Collectors who track value want "highest-cost first", and those who track timeline want "newest acquisition first". Extending `ItemSortMode` to a discriminated union (`{ mode: "default" } | { mode: "name", direction: "asc" | "desc" } | { mode: "cost", direction: "asc" | "desc" } | { mode: "acquired", direction: "asc" | "desc" }`) would unlock all three without touching `applyItemFilters`. The drag-corruption gate already covers any non-default mode.

- **Pin a structural test in `__tests__/item-filters-sort-export-parity.test.ts` that asserts `components/item-filters.tsx` re-exports `applySortMode` + `ItemSortMode` from `lib/item-filters.ts`** — today the re-export is a manual `export { applySortMode }` line; a future contributor who adds a fourth pure helper to `lib/item-filters.ts` could forget to thread it through the component file, silently breaking `@/components/item-filters` consumers. A 1-line grep test would catch the drift the moment it lands.

- **Audit other pure-helper modules for the same "identity path on the no-op input" optimisation** — `applySortMode(items, "default")` returns the input reference unchanged (no allocation) so the upstream `useMemo` equality check holds. The same shape would benefit `applyItemFilters(items, EMPTY_FILTERS)` (today it always returns `items.filter(…)` even when no filter is active — a fresh array every time). A 5-line `if (countActiveFilters(filters) === 0) return items;` short-circuit at the top of the filter loop would close the gap.

### In-collection search UI (2026-05-23)

- **Debounce the `draft.query` keystrokes via a shared `useDebouncedValue(value, 150)` hook before threading them into `onChange(draft)`** — today the search field only takes effect after the user taps Apply, so per-keystroke filtering hasn't been added yet. When the natural next step lands (live-as-you-type filtering directly from the bar without opening the sheet), debouncing protects collections with thousands of items from re-running `applyItemFilters` on every keystroke. A 150ms debounce shim is the standard tradeoff between feeling instant and not thrashing the matcher.

- **Mirror the `searchInCollectionPlaceholder` shape with a `searchInCollectionA11y` accessibility label + `accessibilityRole="search"` on the new TextInput** — VoiceOver currently reads "Search by title, edit text" because the input is unlabeled beyond its placeholder. A 1-key i18n addition + 2 props would close the gap and let blind users discover the search affordance from the sheet structure rather than waiting for the placeholder to be announced after focus.

- **Surface the active `query` as a removable chip in the `ItemFilterBar` quickChips row** — today the search query is invisible until the sheet is reopened, which makes it easy to forget you've narrowed a collection by a stale needle. A "🔎 needle ✕" chip in the horizontal scroll bar (analogous to the existing `resetChip`) would give one-tap clear without the modal round trip and let users see the active narrowing at a glance.

- **Extract the new search-row markup into a reusable `<SheetSearchRow value placeholder onChange />` component** — `app/create.tsx` (collection picker) and `components/item-filters.tsx` (this task) both declare the same `<View><Ionicons name="search"/><TextInput/><Pressable><Ionicons name="close-circle"/></Pressable></View>` shape with near-identical styles. A ~30 LOC component plus a 5-case structural test would let any future sheet (people picker, template picker, marketplace filter) drop in the same affordance without re-implementing it.

- **Add a `__tests__/i18n-translations-no-stale-placeholder.test.ts` audit that asserts every placeholder-typed string ends in a `?`-or-`.`-free phrase shorter than 40 characters** — the new `searchInCollectionPlaceholder` is the 12th placeholder-typed i18n key; without a structural cap, future contributors can drift into long sentences that get truncated on narrow phones (placeholders aren't ellipsised in React Native's `TextInput`). A simple regex/length audit caught at CI time prevents the regression class.

### Home-screen design-tokens migration (2026-05-23)

- **Promote the `[HERO_DARK_4, HERO_DARK, HERO_DARK_5]` triplet to a shared `lib/gradients.ts` constant** — the home screen now declares the same dark gradient as the settings hero. Two duplicated 3-stop arrays is the trigger for extraction: a single `HERO_DARK_GRADIENT` export would let both files import one constant, and the upcoming login-screen-redux migration would close the loop entirely. Pairs naturally with the `withAlpha()` helper for the eventual `OVERLAY_*` family.

- **Extract the `<HeroBanner />` shape into a shared component** — the home screen's hero card (`LinearGradient` + eyebrow + title + profile row + actions row) is the third near-identical hero shape across the codebase (settings, profile detail). A component with optional slots would let those screens use one widget and centralise the `HERO_DARK_GRADIENT` gradient + `MUTED_18` border + `TEXT_ON_DARK_3` title recipe in one file.

- **Extract `<DashboardBanner icon title hint onPress />` from the wishlist + stats banner blocks** — the home screen now declares two near-identical "icon circle + title + hint + arrow" banner blocks (`wishlistBanner` and `statsBanner`) totaling ~80 LOC of style declarations. Extracting them would close the duplication and let the marketplace screen's upcoming "Sales" banner reuse the same widget without re-implementing the recipe.

- **Add a `useDebouncedValue(refreshing, 100)` shim on the home screen's `handleRefresh`** — today the `setRefreshing(true)` toggle flashes the pull-to-refresh indicator even when the underlying `refresh()` promise resolves synchronously (e.g. when offline and the local cache is fresh). A 100ms debounce shim would suppress the brief flash on the happy path while still showing the spinner on real network round trips. Pairs naturally with the `useDebouncedValue` hook suggested for the people-screen search debounce.

- **Pin a `__tests__/index-recent-items.test.ts` that asserts `recentItems` filters out wishlist items AND non-owned collections** — today the `useMemo` does both, but a regression that drops either filter would silently leak wishlist items or shared-collection items into the home dashboard. A small structural test against the memo's inputs/outputs would lock the contract.

### Settings design-tokens migration (2026-05-23)

- **Batch-migrate the new `AMBER_SOFT_3` (`#f0d6a1`) across the 3 remaining inline consumers** — the token now exists but `components/empty-state.tsx` (lines 54 + 66) and `lib/toast-context.tsx` line 120 still inline the value as `borderColor` for the warm-amber accent. Rolling those into a single PR (rather than waiting for the per-file sub-tasks) would lock in its canonical role as "warm amber border" and prevent the value from drifting while someone edits one of those files in isolation.

- **Introduce a cool-palette family (`COOL_GRAY`, `COOL_SLATE`, `COOL_OFFLINE`) for system/diagnostic UI** — `COOL_GRAY = "#94a3b8"` (Tailwind slate-400) is the first cool-tone token in an otherwise warm-brown palette. The off-toggle and any future "neutral / disabled / system status" UI elements should anchor on a small cool-tone family so the warm brown family doesn't grow inconsistently. A 3-token addition (`COOL_GRAY_LIGHT`, `COOL_GRAY`, `COOL_GRAY_DARK`) would give designers a clean "neutral grey" axis without ad-hoc additions.

- **Extract a `<DangerSection>` component** — settings now declares both a "soft danger" pattern (signOutButton: CARD_BG_10 bg + DANGER_SOFT_2 border + DANGER_DEEP_4 text) AND a "danger zone" container (dangerZone: CARD_BG_11 bg + DANGER_SOFT_3 border + DANGER_DEEP_5 title + DANGER_MEDIUM body + DANGER_DEEP_2 deleteButton). The same recipe will recur on any future "destructive flow" screen (collection delete, profile delete, premium cancel). Extracting `<DangerSection title hint actionLabel onAction tone={"soft"|"hard"} />` would let those screens import one widget with token-aware styling.

- **Pin a `__tests__/design-tokens-danger-family.test.ts` luminance-monotonicity test** — with `DANGER` / `DANGER_DEEP` / `_2` / `_3` / `_4` / `_5` and `DANGER_SOFT` / `_2` / `_3` now spanning 9 distinct red shades, the suffix numbering should be enforced structurally (deeper = lower luminance, softer = higher luminance). A simple helper that converts each token to YIQ luminance and asserts strict monotonic ordering would catch a future contributor accidentally inserting `DANGER_DEEP_6 = "#ff8888"` (lighter, breaking the family convention). Same shape would extend to `MUTED_*`, `HERO_DARK_*`, `CARD_BG_*` once we ship the helper.

- **Replace the LinearGradient `colors={[HERO_DARK_4, HERO_DARK, HERO_DARK_5]}` triplet with a named `lib/gradients.ts` constant** — the settings hero now declares a 3-stop dark gradient that the login screen and onboarding flow are likely to reuse. A single `HERO_DARK_GRADIENT = [HERO_DARK_4, HERO_DARK, HERO_DARK_5] as const` exported from `lib/gradients.ts` would let those screens import one constant instead of re-declaring the triplet. Pairs with a `withAlpha()` helper for the eventual `OVERLAY_*` family.

### Item-filters design-tokens migration (2026-05-23)

- **Batch-migrate the new `DANGER_DEEP_4` / `DANGER_SOFT_2` / `CARD_BG_10` "soft destructive chip" trio across the 5 remaining inline consumers** — the trio now lives inline in `app/settings.tsx` (3 occurrences) and `app/collection/[id].tsx` (4 occurrences). Each uses the same `paddingHorizontal/Vertical + borderRadius:999 + CARD_BG_10 bg + DANGER_SOFT_2 border + DANGER_DEEP_4 fg` recipe to render a "soft destructive action" chip. Rolling them in a single PR (rather than waiting for the per-file sub-tasks 2+ tasks away) would lock in the canonical chip styling and prevent a future contributor from inlining `#d9a0a1` (off by one in the green channel).

- **Extract a shared `<SoftDestructiveChip />` component from the resetChip recipe** — item-filters now declares the exact "icon + label, pale red bg/border, deep red fg" shape that the settings screen and collection screen replicate inline. A single `<SoftDestructiveChip icon label onPress />` component would let those screens import one widget instead of re-implementing the 4-line stylesheet, and gives the danger family its first composite "soft destructive action" UI primitive (sibling to the `<DangerIconButton />` extraction logged in the wishlist suggestions). Pairs naturally with the `__tests__/design-tokens-danger-family.test.ts` luminance assertion.

- **Add a `<FilterBar />` integration test that mounts the component with an active filter and asserts the rendered `resetChip` color matches `DANGER_DEEP_4`** — pinning rendered styles against imported token constants would catch any future regression where a contributor accidentally re-introduces an inline hex literal that compiles fine but skips visual review. Same shape as the chat detail / search-overlay integration test suggestions; centralising them in a `__tests__/design-tokens-rendering.test.ts` suite would let each file's adoption test cover both source-level + runtime assertions.

- **Persist the `ItemFilters` draft across modal open/close so partial input isn't lost on accidental backdrop tap** — today the filter modal resets `draft` to the current `filters` on every `openModal()` call, but the *current* `filters` snapshot is itself stale if the user opened the modal, typed a partial price, then tapped the backdrop instead of "Apply". A `useEffect(() => setDraft(filters), [filters])` (rather than the open-side reset) would keep the draft sticky until "Reset" is pressed. The change is 2 lines and removes a footgun the design team has called out as confusing.

- **Add `keyboardType="numeric"` enforcement + min/max validation to the `priceFrom`/`priceTo` `TextInput`s** — today the inputs accept any string and the apply step calls `parseFloat` which can return NaN or negative numbers. A pure `validatePriceRange(from, to)` helper in `lib/filter-helpers.ts` would let the apply button gray out on invalid input (e.g. `from > to` or non-numeric) and surface a `t("filterInvalidPrice")` hint below the row, mirroring the existing `inputInvalid` style from `create-collection.tsx`.

Extracting it would let those screens use one component instead of re-implementing the 4-line stylesheet, and gives the danger family its first composite "destructive action" UI primitive.

Same shape would extend to `MUTED_*`, `HERO_DARK_*`, `CARD_BG_*` once we ship a similar density helper.

Centralising it would also let the eventual "trade mode = green accent" rebrand be a one-line edit instead of a sweep.

- **Batch-migrate the new `AMBER_MUTED_3` (`#d8c7b1`) across the remaining 3 inline consumers** — the value now lives inline in `components/item-card.tsx` (2 occurrences) and `app/marketplace.tsx`. Each treats `#d8c7b1` as the photo-fallback fill; rolling those into a single PR (rather than waiting for the per-file sub-tasks 4+ tasks away) would prevent the value from drifting to `#d8c7b0` while someone edits one of those screens in isolation. ~5 minutes per file, fully mechanical.

- **Batch-migrate the new `HERO_DARK_7` (`#2a1e17`) and `TEXT_ON_DARK_6` (`#fff7ed`) pair across `app/item/[id].tsx` and `app/settings.tsx`** — both tokens appear together as the "dark hero card + cream-on-dark text" recipe in the item detail and settings header. Rolling them in now (one ~5-line PR per file) would close the visual loop before each screen's larger migration sub-task lands, and let those tasks focus on the *new* hex values they introduce instead.

- **Promote the `<OwnerChip />` (avatar + label + name + handle) shape into a shared component** — `app/listing/[id].tsx`, `app/profile/[id].tsx`, and the marketplace card grid render conceptually-identical "user attribution chip" blocks with 6 styles each (`ownerChip`, `ownerAvatar`, `ownerAvatarFallback`, `ownerAvatarText`, `ownerLabel`, `ownerName`, `ownerHandle`). Extracting it would eliminate ~40 LOC across each consumer and let the new `AMBER_MUTED` + `HERO_DARK_3` + `MUTED` + `TEXT_DARK` tokens have exactly one consumer site.

- **Add a `<ModeBadge mode />` extraction so the `paddingHorizontal/Vertical + borderRadius: 999 + AMBER_ACCENT|SUCCESS_GREEN ternary` recipe lives in one component** — listing detail declares both a `modeBadge` (larger) and `priceHistoryModeBadge` (smaller) with the same color contract. A `<ModeBadge mode size?: "sm" | "md" />` component would let `app/marketplace.tsx`, `app/item/[id].tsx`, and the future "Sales" subsection share the styling without duplicating the conditional. Pairs naturally with the `modeAccentColor()` helper suggested above.

### Create-collection design-tokens migration (2026-05-23)

- **Batch-migrate the new `AMBER_MUTED_2` (`#dbc7ae`) across the remaining 4 inline consumers** — the value now lives inline in `components/photo-preview.tsx`, `app/wishlist.tsx`, `app/index.tsx`, `app/collection/[id].tsx`. Each of these uses `#dbc7ae` as an image-placeholder background; rolling those into a single PR (rather than waiting for the per-file sub-tasks several tasks away) would lock in its canonical role as "warm tan image-placeholder fill" and prevent the value from drifting to `#dbc7af` while someone edits one of those screens in isolation. ~5 minutes per file, fully mechanical.

- **Batch-migrate the new `TEXT_DARK_4` (`#2b2017`) across the remaining 2 inline consumers** — the value now lives inline in `app/create.tsx` (3 occurrences) and `app/item/[id].tsx`. The semantic role ("display-heading dark brown") is already shared by all four call sites; centralising the value before those screens are migrated would let their per-file sweeps focus on the *new* hex values they introduce instead of reasoning about which `_4` suffix to pick.

- **Batch-migrate the new `MUTED_17` (`#7a6453`) across the remaining 2 inline consumers** — the value lives inline in `components/photo-preview.tsx` and `app/collection/[id].tsx` (2 occurrences). All four sites use it as a muted-brown hint/secondary-text color; landing the rename now prevents a future contributor from inlining `#7a6452` (off by one in the green channel — invisible to the eye, invisible to git blame, but breaks the single-source-of-truth contract).

- **Extract a `<HeroBanner>` component shared by `create-collection.tsx` and `create.tsx`** — both screens render a near-identical hero card (`backgroundColor: CARD_BG_5`, `borderRadius: 28`, `padding: 20`, title + subtitle). The create-item screen's hero will land its own `CARD_BG_5` consumer in the next migration sub-task; deduplicating the shape into `components/hero-banner.tsx` would let the rest of the codebase use one cited component rather than re-implementing the visual recipe each time.

- **Add a `templates` empty-state hint when `collectionTemplates` is filtered to zero results** — the current screen renders an empty horizontal `ScrollView` when no templates match (e.g. a future user-locale filter), with no visible indication of *why* nothing shows. A 4-line conditional rendering `t("noTemplatesAvailable")` would close the UX gap; the i18n key would map naturally onto the existing `coverFallbackHint` pattern. Pairs with a feature flag for "personalised templates" if/when that lands.

### People design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Extract `<Pagination>` into a shared component** — `app/people.tsx` declares 6 pagination-related styles (`pagination`, `pageButton`, `pageButtonDisabled`, `pageButtonText`, `pageButtonTextDisabled`, `pageInfo`) for a widget the marketplace, wishlist, and acquired-items screens all want. Extracting a `<Pagination page total onPageChange />` component would let the new `BORDER_4` + `MUTED_16` tokens have exactly one consumer site (semantically: "disabled-button styling") instead of every screen re-wiring them.

- **Promote the `<ProfileActionCard />` extraction (already suggested in the friends migration suggestions) before migrating `app/profile/[id].tsx` (40 hex literals, the next big-ticket file in the queue)** — both screens render the same "card + avatar + meta + 1-2 pill buttons" shape with friend/follow/request states. Extracting it now means the profile migration becomes a one-line component update for the action-row instead of yet another full-file sweep. The people screen's `renderProfileCard` is the cleaner reference implementation.

- **Add an a11y label to the disabled pagination button stating "previous page disabled" / "next page disabled"** — today the buttons gray out with `disabled={page <= 1}` but expose no screen-reader hint about why they're disabled, which fails WCAG 4.1.2. The fix is a 2-line conditional inside the existing `<Pressable>`. Pairs naturally with the `<Pagination>` extraction above.

- **Switch the people-screen search debounce from synchronous `setQuery` to a 200ms `useDebouncedValue(query, 200)` hook** — the screen currently re-filters the entire `others` array on every keystroke. With ~100 profiles loaded (the current page size) the cost is negligible, but as the directory grows past a few hundred users the per-keystroke filter will become user-visible jank on older Android devices. A debounce hook in `lib/use-debounced-value.ts` would also be reusable by search-overlay and future filter screens.

- **Add an integration test that asserts the `pageButtonDisabled` background is `BORDER_4` and the `pageButtonTextDisabled` color is `MUTED_16`** — pinning the disabled-state styling against the imported token constants would catch any future regression where someone re-introduces an inline hex while editing the pagination markup. Same shape as the chat detail / search-overlay integration test suggestions; centralising them in a `__tests__/design-tokens-rendering.test.ts` suite would let each file's adoption test cover both the source-level assertion (no inline hex) and the runtime assertion (rendered token matches).

### Search-overlay design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Batch-migrate `MUTED_15` (`#b8a08a`) across the other 2 inline consumers (`app/create.tsx` + `components/item-filters.tsx`) in one sweep** — the token now exists but its other call sites still inline the value; rolling those into a single PR (rather than waiting for the per-file sub-tasks 5+ tasks away) would lock in its canonical role as "light-muted-brown clear/close icon" and prevent the value from drifting to `#b8a18a` while someone edits one of those screens in isolation.

- **Extract the search-overlay backdrop (`rgba(38, 27, 20, 0.55)`) into a shared `OVERLAY_BACKDROP` token** — the same semi-transparent dark cream appears in the bottom-nav modal and would appear in every future overlay sheet. The existing 6-digit token convention can't represent alpha; a separate `OVERLAY_BACKDROP` (or a `withAlpha(HERO_DARK, 0.55)` helper that derives it at module-evaluation time) would centralise the value without breaking the hex-shape contract on the rest of the palette.

- **Promote the filter-chip / owner-chip pair into a shared `<FilterChip />` component** — search-overlay declares two near-identical chip variants (filter vs. owner) with subtly different padding and text color. Extracting a single component with `variant: "primary" | "ghost"` would let `app/create.tsx`, `app/marketplace.tsx`, and `components/item-filters.tsx` (which already render conceptually-similar chips) deduplicate ~40 LOC apiece while the token mapping lives in one file.

- **Add a `search-overlay.tsx` integration test that mounts the component with a mocked CollectionsProvider and asserts the active-filter chip's `backgroundColor` equals `HERO_DARK`** — pinning rendered styles against imported token constants would catch any future regression where a contributor accidentally re-introduces an inline hex literal that compiles fine but skips visual review. Same shape as the chat detail integration test suggestion.

- **Wire a `__tests__/design-tokens-density.test.ts` that ranks every migrated file by `(unique-hex-literals-before / unique-tokens-used-after)` ratio** — search-overlay landed at 19 inline values mapping to 19 unique tokens (1:1 — no consolidation opportunity), but later migrations (e.g. `app/collection/[id].tsx` with 86 hex literals) likely have far more duplicated values per file. Surfacing the ratio in CI output would help the design team identify "good consolidation candidates" (high ratio = many duplicated inline values that could collapse onto one token) before each migration sub-task lands.

### Chat detail design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Batch-migrate the new `TEXT_ON_DARK_5` (`#fff7ea`) across the remaining 6 inline consumers** — the value now lives inline in `app/create.tsx`, `app/settings.tsx`, `app/wishlist.tsx`, `app/index.tsx`, `components/selectable-item-row.tsx`, `components/empty-state.tsx`, `components/item-filters.tsx`. The chat migration introduced the token but only swept its first call site; landing the rename across the other six in a single PR (rather than waiting for each per-file sub-task) would lock in its canonical role as "primary cream-on-dark button/icon foreground" and prevent the value from drifting to `#fff7eb` while someone edits one of those screens in isolation.

- **Promote the offline-pill widget (`offlinePill` + `offlinePillText` styles) into a shared `<RealtimeOfflinePill />` component** — the same "warm cream pill with dark-amber text" pattern is the natural rendering target for the `RealtimeStatusProvider` consumers added in the marketplace status work. Today the pill is duplicated in chat detail + the registered `<RealtimeStatusPill />` component; deduplicating into a single token-driven component means any future palette tweak to the warning state is a one-line edit.

- **Extract the message-bubble pair (`bubble` / `bubbleMine` / `bubbleTheirs` + the four text variants) into a `<ChatBubble mine={…} text={…} time={…} />` component** — once the chat screen grows reactions, edited indicators, or read receipts, the inline bubble markup will need surgery in N places; a single shared component keeps the token mapping in one file and makes a future Tailwind-style design pass tractable.

- **Add a `chat/[id].tsx` integration test that mounts the screen with a mocked ChatProvider and asserts the empty state, typing-row, offline pill, and disabled-send-button each render with their expected token-driven background colors** — the chat detail screen is the highest-traffic synchronous-interaction surface but has no behavioural tests today. Pinning the rendered backgroundColor via `findAllByType(View)` against the imported token constants would catch any future regression where a contributor accidentally re-introduces an inline hex literal that compiles but skips the visual review.

- **Rename `MUTED_12 = "#7a4f1a"` to a semantic `WARN_TEXT` token** — the chat migration named it ordinally for consistency with the rest of the palette, but its role (warning text on warm cream pill) is categorical, not positional. The next palette refactor will likely keep the value but want the name to reflect its semantic role (mirroring the existing `STATUS_ONLINE` / `STATUS_OFFLINE` naming break from the ordinal convention). A rename + `RealtimeOfflinePill` extraction would land naturally as one PR.

### Currency conversion for total cost (2026-05-22)

- **Surface a currency picker in `app/item/[id].tsx` (item edit) so users can correct a wrong-currency entry without deleting and re-adding the item.** Today only `app/create.tsx` exposes the picker — an item created in USD that should have been EUR is locked unless the user deletes it. The picker UI already exists; rewiring it under the existing cost field in the edit modal is ~30 LOC.

- **Add a tiny "rates unavailable" pill on cards / detail pages when `currencyRates === null` AND items carry mixed currencies.** Today the fallback summation treats all items as if they were already in `displayCurrency`, which is silently wrong for mixed-currency collections during the first paint or when the API is down. The context already exposes the data (`getCollectionTotalCost(id).skipped > 0` or the rates state), but the UI doesn't distinguish the two states.

- **Switch `getCollectionTotalCost`'s fallback from "assume all items in displayCurrency" to "return null amount + a `pending: true` flag"** — the caller could then render `--` instead of a wrong number. Today the fallback (`reduce(... + e.amount, 0)`) over-reports for mixed-currency collections during the rates-loading window; an explicit pending state would also unlock a skeleton placeholder.

- **Add a manual "Refresh rates" entry in `app/settings.tsx`** that calls the new `refreshCurrencyRates()` from `CollectionsContext` so power users can force a refresh after a known FX move without waiting 24h. The wiring is 5 lines (Pressable + toast) since the context already exposes the action.

- **Move the rate fetch into `lib/auth-context.tsx`'s sign-in success path** so rates are warmed once when the session resolves rather than on every CollectionsProvider mount. Today the rates effect re-runs on app cold-start; gating it on the auth session would avoid an unnecessary fetch on the offline sign-out path and would let a future "premium tier" gate the higher-precision rate source behind an entitlement check.

### Friends design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Batch-migrate `MUTED_10` (`#624a35`) across the other 7 inline consumers in one sweep** — the value now lives inline in `components/search-overlay.tsx`, `app/people.tsx`, `components/item-filters.tsx`, `app/create-collection.tsx`, `app/create.tsx`, `app/collection/[id].tsx`, `app/item/[id].tsx`. Doing the token-rename in a single PR (rather than waiting for each file's per-task sub-task) would lock in its canonical role as "uppercase section-label brown" and prevent someone drifting the value to e.g. `#604a36` while editing one of those screens in isolation.

- **Extract the chats-link card (lines 126-141) into a shared `<ChatsLinkCard unread={n} />` component** — the same widget (icon + title/subtitle + unread badge / chevron-forward) is already very close to what would live in profile screens, account headers, and the marketplace dashboard once those screens grow chat hooks. Extracting it now keeps the design-token mapping in one place and centralises the unread-badge color contract before the friends/marketplace/profile triples it.

- **Replace the `chatsBadge` `color: "#fff"` 3-digit shorthand with `TEXT_ON_DARK` (or a new `WHITE_PURE_SHORT` token)** — keeping shorthand as an escape hatch from the 6-digit regex is a slippery slope; eventually one of the design-tokens-adoption tests should also fail on 3-digit literals, and the friends/chats badges should be the first to migrate. The trade-off is that `TEXT_ON_DARK = #fff7ef` is slightly cream — a tiny perceptual difference on a red badge but worth a design-led call before flipping it.

- **Promote the friend/follow/request "card with two pill buttons" row into a `<ProfileActionCard profile={p} kind={…} />` component** — `app/friends.tsx`'s `renderProfileCard` already encodes three kinds (`friend` / `following` / `request`) with two-button or one-button variants. The same pattern shows up in `app/people.tsx` and `app/profile/[id].tsx` (with subtly different button copy / actions). Extracting it would let the token migration of those two files become a one-line component update instead of another full-file sweep.

- **Add a `friends.tsx` integration test that mounts the screen with a mocked SocialProvider and asserts the empty state, friend list, and incoming-request list each render with their expected accessibility labels** — the friends screen is the highest-traffic social surface but has no behavioural tests today. A test that pins the tab labels, section headers, and primary-action button copy per-locale would catch any future regression in the friends-vs-following swap (esp. when the `dotHighlight` logic ships per-locale variations).

### Layout design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

Either (a) align them to a single token `SPLASH_BG` referenced by both files via a build-time codegen step, or (b) document the intentional gradient between splash and shell. A `__tests__/splash-shell-bg-parity.test.ts` that reads app.json and asserts the value matches a documented constant would prevent silent drift the next time someone edits one without the other.

- **Batch-migrate `ACCENT_DEEP` (`#8a5a2b`) across 4 other consumers** — `app/auth/callback.tsx:92`, `app/item/[id].tsx:1062`, `components/screen.tsx:27` all inline the same value today. A token-anchored sweep would lock in its canonical role as "refresh/loading spinner color" before someone drifts the value during a later per-file migration.

- **Promote `STATUS_ONLINE` / `STATUS_OFFLINE` into a semantic `realtimeStatusColor(state)` helper in `lib/realtime-status-context.tsx`** — the layout currently encodes the mapping inline (`realtimeOnline ? styles.realtimeDotOnline : styles.realtimeDotOffline`); the helper would let `components/realtime-status-pill.tsx` (shipped two tasks ago) share the same color contract instead of duplicating it. Today the pill renders text only — adding a colored dot in the pill that matches the header dot is a one-line follow-up once the helper exists.

Extracting it would let the migration of those colors live in one place and would centralise the "checking session" UX language for future polish (skeleton instead of spinner, themed-spinner palette, etc.).

Extracting a `<HeaderChatsButton />` component would halve the JSX and would let the future "show pill instead of dot at small widths" iteration touch one site.

### Swipe-tabs design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Audit `MUTED_2` (`#6b5647`) and `MUTED_8` (`#6b5543`) for unification** — the two tokens differ only in the last byte (47 vs 43), almost imperceptible visually. A perceptual-distance test (CIE-Lab ΔE under 1.5) would let a future refactor consolidate them safely, or document that the difference is intentional (e.g. one is "muted on cream", the other is "muted on amber"). Today neither file calls out the distinction.

- **Replace the `{...styles.tab, ...(isActive ? styles.tabActive : {})}` style spreads with array form** — `components/swipe-tabs.tsx` rebuilds 4 style objects (`tab`, `tabText`, `subTab`, `subTabText`) on every render of every tab. RN's `style={[styles.tab, isActive && styles.tabActive]}` short-circuits cleanly on `false` and keeps StyleSheet identity-equality intact. Tiny perf win on a hot interactive widget.

- **Add a `<DotRow>` sub-component for the indicator dots** — the inline `tabs.map((t, i) => <View …/>)` block at lines 205-218 mixes three style-merge concerns (dot, dotActive/subDotActive, dotHighlight). Extracting it to a typed sub-component `<DotRow tabs={tabs} activeIndex={i} variant={…} highlight={…} />` would clean up the JSX, make each style-merge concern testable in isolation, and let designers iterate on the dot row independently.

- **Move `ANIM_DURATION = 220` into a `lib/animation-tokens.ts` family** — alongside any future timing constants. Today the swipe-tabs animation duration is a magic number embedded in the file; pulling it into a sibling module to design-tokens would let an accessibility-first reduced-motion pass flip every transition duration from one file.

- **Render the swipe-tabs widget inside a future `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` preview** — the widget exercises six tokens (`HERO_DARK`, `AMBER_ACCENT`, `AMBER_SOFT`, `CARD_BG_3`, `TEXT_ON_DARK_4`, `MUTED_3`) plus 4 interactive states (idle/active/highlight, sub vs main variant). Including it would let designers verify the full tab-row contrast story on one row of the swatch grid.

### Login-screen design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Batch-migrate the 3 other files using the `[HERO_DARK_4, HERO_DARK, HERO_DARK_5]` gradient** — the exact same `colors={["#3d2810", "#261b14", "#1e140e"]}` 3-stop now lives inline in `app/settings.tsx:95` and `app/index.tsx:98` after this task. A single token-anchored sweep replacing those 3 inline copies with the new tokens (vs. waiting for their per-file sub-tasks in `.tasks.md`) would lock in the canonical hero-gradient signature before someone duplicates a near-but-not-identical 3-stop (`#3d2911`, `#1e150e`) and the brand visually splits across screens.

- **Batch-migrate `#fff4e8` (`TEXT_ON_DARK_4`) across the 9 files using it inline** — it's the most-shared token shipped in this batch (search-overlay, swipe-tabs, item-filters, people, _layout, settings, friends, collection, profile). Doing them all in one sweep keeps the "cream-on-dark button text" semantics consistent and prevents the same drift risk above.

- **Add a `DANGER_DEEP` semantic alias `FORM_ERROR_TEXT`** — `#a13434` is named today as a darker red but its only consumer is form-error text under inputs. A semantic alias `export const FORM_ERROR_TEXT = DANGER_DEEP;` would make call-site intent explicit and would let designers tune error-message contrast separately from destructive-button reds (which use `DANGER`).

- **Promote the `…{...styles.primaryButton, ...(pending ? styles.disabledButton : {})}` spread to `[styles.primaryButton, pending && styles.disabledButton]`** — the four button Pressables in `components/login-screen.tsx` build a brand-new style object on every render. RN's style-array API short-circuits cleanly on `false` and gives StyleSheet identity-equality the chance to skip a re-flatten. Free perf win on the auth screen specifically (it re-renders during the OTP flow).

- **Add an `__tests__/login-screen-gradient.test.ts` that pins the 3-stop colors to the token names, not the values** — today the no-inline-hex assertion catches that no literal remains, but a future renaming of `HERO_DARK_4` (e.g. to `HERO_DARK_TOP`) without updating the import in `login-screen.tsx` would slip through. Asserting the `<LinearGradient colors={[HERO_DARK_4, HERO_DARK, HERO_DARK_5]}>` shape (rather than just the presence of the imports) would close the rename-drift gap.

### Stats design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Batch-migrate the 9 other files now also using `TEXT_DARK_3` (`#2d2117`)** — the token currently appears inline in `app/create.tsx`, `app/index.tsx`, `app/profile/[id].tsx`, `app/collection/[id].tsx`, `app/item/[id].tsx`, `components/item-filters.tsx`. Each is already in the decomposed `.tasks.md` migration backlog, but doing a single token-anchored sweep (vs. file-by-file) would lock in `#2d2117`'s canonical role as "summary numeric/highlight text" before a near-but-different value (`#2d2118`, `#2e2117`) creeps in and quietly splits the palette.

- **Add an `Intl.NumberFormat` currency-aware total in stats** — `totalValue.toLocaleString()` formats the bare number but doesn't render a currency symbol; the items each carry `costCurrency` (`USD` / `EUR` / …) so the screen could group sums per currency and render via `Intl.NumberFormat(getDefaultLocaleForLanguage(language), { style: "currency", currency }).format(sum)`. Today the user sees "10000" instead of "$10,000.00", which is a real readability regression on the stats screen specifically (where the value is the headline).

- **Wire a chart accent palette and a "chart pill colors should stay raw" guard** — the original task description anticipated a multi-color chart palette that should NOT migrate to brand tokens, but the current stats screen is a single-bar chart so the caveat went unexercised. The next chart (e.g. a category breakdown pie/donut) will need 6–8 non-brand colors; adding a `lib/chart-palette.ts` now with documented "intentionally not in design-tokens" framing + a regex assert that the file lives outside `lib/design-tokens.ts` would document the boundary before the first multi-color chart is implemented.

- **Refactor the bar-chart math into a pure `bucketItemsByMonth(items, monthsBack)` helper in `lib/stats.ts`** — the `useMemo` block in `app/stats.tsx:32-44` is 13 lines of pure date-bucketing logic that would test cleanly in isolation (today there's no `__tests__/stats-growth.test.ts`). Extracting it would let a future analytics dashboard reuse the same bucketing without re-implementing the `padStart(2, "0")` / `slice(-12)` / `localeCompare` dance, and would unblock writing the empty-state / single-item / DST-boundary test cases the screen's growth chart relies on.

- **Replace the `barFill` style spread (`{ ...styles.barFill, height: `${…}%` }`) with `[styles.barFill, { height }]`** at `app/stats.tsx:83-86` — RN's array-style API is the idiomatic way to merge a static style with a dynamic prop; the spread form allocates a new object on every render of every bar and bypasses StyleSheet's identity-equality optimisation. Tiny but free perf win on a screen that renders up to 12 bars × 1 hot effect each refresh.

### Chats design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Migrate the four other files using `AMBER_MUTED` in one batch** — `#d9c2a8` is now also live in `components/search-overlay.tsx:501`, `app/people.tsx:263`, `app/friends.tsx:316`, and `app/listing/[id].tsx:382`. Migrating them together (vs. doing them per-file in the existing decomposed sub-tasks) would lock in the token's canonical role (avatar/empty-state fallback bg) before a future inline-hex regression introduces a near-but-not-identical value (`#d9c2a9`, `#d8c2a8` etc.) and quietly splits the palette.

- **Migrate `color: "#fff"` (3-digit shorthand) too** — the no-inline-hex adoption test only catches the 6-digit form, but `#fff` / `#000` shorthand still bypasses the token system. A second assertion in the adoption helper `assert.deepEqual(src.match(/#[0-9a-fA-F]{3}\b/g) ?? [], [])` (boundary-anchored to avoid matching the start of 6-digit literals) would close the gap; today only `app/chats.tsx`'s badge text uses `#fff`, so a single migration to a new `PURE_WHITE` token (or a justification to leave it) clears the codebase.
