- **Promote `HERO_DARK_3` to `HERO_AVATAR_TEXT` (semantic alias)** — `#3a2716` originally entered the palette as a hero variant but its only consumer in `app/chats.tsx` is the avatar fallback letter color. A semantic alias `export const HERO_AVATAR_TEXT = HERO_DARK_3;` would make consumer intent explicit at the call site, and would let designers darken/lighten avatar text without thinking about whether the value is also wired into a hero background.

- **Add a `chats-hero` story to the future `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` preview** — the chats hero exercises four cream-on-dark tokens (`AMBER_LIGHT` eyebrow, `TEXT_ON_DARK_3` title, `TEXT_ON_DARK_SOFT` subtitle, `HERO_DARK` bg) on one compact widget. Including it would let designers verify the full hero contrast story on one row of the swatch grid; same logic that landed bottom-nav's preview suggestion last task.

- **Audit the three existing `TEXT_ON_DARK*` variants** — the palette now ships TEXT_ON_DARK (#fff7ef), TEXT_ON_DARK_2 (#fff5ea), and TEXT_ON_DARK_3 (#fff8ef). The three colors are visually nearly indistinguishable; only the design-system contract that "each surface owns one variant" justifies keeping them separate. A `__tests__/design-tokens-perceptual.test.ts` that asserts the pairwise CIE-Lab ΔE between TEXT_ON_DARK variants stays under some threshold would document the visual relationship and let a future palette refactor consolidate them safely.

### Nav-tab design-tokens migration (2026-05-22)

- **Promote `MUTED_4` (the new `#bbb0a6` inactive-nav-icon token) to a semantic alias `ICON_INACTIVE`** — `MUTED_4` is named by its position in the muted-brown ramp, not by its role. A second named export `export const ICON_INACTIVE = MUTED_4;` (or a renamed token with `MUTED_4` kept as a back-compat alias) would make consumer intent self-documenting at the call site (`color={item.active ? ICON_ACTIVE : ICON_INACTIVE}`), and would let designers raise/lower contrast on inactive icons without thinking about whether the value is also wired into a non-icon muted-text surface.

- **Move `Ionicons size={22}` into a `lib/design-tokens.ts` numeric scale** — every nav icon hard-codes `22` for the icon size and `4/8/10/18` for badge dimensions; the design-tokens module today only covers colors. Extending it with `ICON_SIZE_NAV`, `BADGE_DOT_SIZE`, `BADGE_COUNT_HEIGHT`, etc. would mirror the existing color migration pattern and let an accessibility pass (larger tap targets) flip everything from one file. Listed adjacent to the existing `.tasks.md` line 88 "semantic spacing/radius tokens" task — same shape, sized one notch smaller.

- **Add a `tokens-coverage` audit script** — `npm run audit:design-tokens` could grep every `.tsx` under `app/`+`components/` for `#[0-9a-fA-F]{6}` and fail the build (or emit a count) if the total exceeds a baseline. Today the decomposed migration list in `.tasks.md` hard-codes the per-file count from a manual sweep done weeks ago; an automated counter would update those numbers in CI and surface drift the moment a new contributor re-introduces a literal.

- **Render `<NavTab>` inside the future `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` preview** (already a `.tasks.md` backlog item) — the badge dot, premium dot, and active dot together exercise four tokens (`HERO_DARK`, `DANGER`, `AMBER_ACCENT`, `TEXT_ON_DARK`) on one compact widget. Including the tab in the preview would let designers verify the full bottom-nav contrast story (active + inactive + badge + premium) on one row of the swatch grid.

- **Migrate the inline `Ionicons` `color={…}` prop in every screen header (`app/chats.tsx`, `app/friends.tsx`, `app/people.tsx`, etc.) using the same `HERO_DARK`/`MUTED_4` active-vs-inactive pair** — most header icons today hard-code `#261b14` for the active icon and a separate hex for the inactive state; standardising on the nav-tab's token pair would mean a single design-tokens edit re-skins the entire icon system, not just the bottom nav.

### Bottom-nav design-tokens migration (2026-05-21)

- **Add a `palette-coverage` test that asserts every hex value used by `bottom-nav.tsx` matches an exported token, not just that the *names* are imported** — today the adoption test pins token *names* (`HERO_DARK`, `CARD_BG_2`, etc.) and the no-inline-hex assertion catches the absence of literals, but a future refactor that renames `TEXT_ON_DARK_2` while leaving the value `#fff5ea` inline would slip through. A snapshot check `assert.equal(parseStyle(bottomNavSrc).modalPrimaryText.color, TEXT_ON_DARK_2)` would close the rename-drift gap.

- **Extract the `rgba(20, 12, 6, 0.55)` modal backdrop into a `BACKDROP_DARK` token** with a parallel `withAlpha(token, 0.55)` helper. The backdrop is the only color in `bottom-nav.tsx` that *isn't* in the palette today; standardising it as a token (plus an alpha helper) would let any future "darken on overlay" surface (image preview overlays, photo-edit modes) share one source of truth instead of each modal hard-coding its own rgba quartet.

- **Migrate `components/nav-tab.tsx` next** — it's the sibling of `bottom-nav.tsx` (rendered as `<NavTab>` inside the `NavRow`) and carries 9 inline hex literals. Doing the two together would mean the entire bottom-nav surface re-skins from a single design-tokens edit; today only the wrapper migrated.

- **Add a `bottom-nav` story to the future `app/_dev/tokens.tsx` preview route** (already on `.tasks.md` line 70) — rendering the actual `BottomNav` next to a swatch grid of the 9 tokens it consumes would make the rotation argument concrete for designers reviewing palette changes. The preview route is on the backlog; pre-staging the bottom-nav fixture means it can be the first concrete example when the route lands.

- **Surface a TypeScript-friendly `bottomNavStyles` factory** — `bottom-nav.tsx` now references 9 tokens scattered across its `StyleSheet.create({...})`. A factory `createBottomNavStyles(tokens)` that takes the palette as a parameter would let the same component render in two themes (e.g. a future high-contrast a11y mode) without forking the file. The migration just unlocked this — every token is now a named import instead of a literal, so threading a `tokens` arg through is one refactor away.

### Social-context realtime invariant guardrail (2026-05-21)

- **Extend the realtime-invariant guard to every consumer file** — the test currently only protects `lib/social-context.tsx`. The same pattern (`no new RealtimeClient`, `no inline channel.subscribe`, `must import from @/lib/supabase-realtime`) applies to every future cloud-backed module: `lib/premium-context.tsx`, `lib/collections-context.tsx`, `lib/marketplace-context.tsx`, `lib/chat-context.tsx`. A parameterized helper `assertSharedRealtimeInvariant(filePath)` exported from a new `__tests__/_helpers/realtime-invariant.ts` would let one wiring test cover all five files with a single `forEach`. Today each file would need its own bespoke test that copy-pastes the four regexes.

- **Promote the invariant into an ESLint rule** — structural tests catch the regression in CI but won't surface it in the editor before commit. A custom rule `collectables/no-direct-realtime-client` (or a `no-restricted-imports` config for `@supabase/realtime-js` outside the allowlisted `lib/supabase-realtime.ts` + `lib/realtime-channel-registry.ts` paths) would give the same protection with a red squiggle in VS Code. Mirrors the design-tokens-lint-rule suggestion already on `.tasks.md` line 66 — same problem shape, same solution.

- **Add a `social-context.tsx` presence prototype guarded behind a flag** — the task framing was "once realtime ships in social-context, route through the shared client." That moment can be brought forward by wiring up a behind-the-flag presence channel (e.g. a `friends:online` topic that emits `friendId -> online` events keyed off `EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_SOCIAL_PRESENCE=1`). Even an empty stub that calls `subscribeShared` then `unsubscribe`s would exercise the integration path and let `RealtimeStatusProvider` surface "social channel reconnecting" pills without changing the user-facing UI.

- **Render the `topics` Map snapshot in a `__DEV__`-gated overlay** — once social-context starts publishing channels, the `useRealtimeStatus().topics` map becomes the single source of truth for "which sockets does this device have open right now?" An overlay component `<RealtimeTopicsDebugOverlay />` (mounted in `app/_layout.tsx` behind `__DEV__`) would render the live topic list with each entry's `connected: boolean`, giving engineers an in-app analog of the Chrome Network panel's WS view without leaving the app.

- **Add a one-shot reconnect test that exercises social + chat + marketplace simultaneously** — the registry's WeakMap-per-client design already isolates topics, but no test today walks the full "three contexts subscribing to the same shared client, then status emits propagate to all three" flow. A small integration test in `__tests__/registry-multi-consumer-status.test.ts` that registers three fake handlers on three topics and asserts the snapshot reflects all three would catch a regression where the WeakMap accidentally collapses entries from different contexts.

### Shared realtime status context (2026-05-21)

- **Reuse `<RealtimeStatusPill />` in `app/chat/[id].tsx`** — the chat screen still renders its own inline `{allowed && !realtimeOnline ? <View style={styles.offlinePill}> … </View> : null}` block driven by `useChat().realtimeOnline`. Now that the shared pill is wired and the inbox channel publishes status into the registry, the chat-context-local `realtimeOnline` state is redundant. Swap the inline pill for `<RealtimeStatusPill topic={inboxChannelTopic(user.id)} />` (after adding the optional `topic` prop that defaults to the aggregate), then remove `setRealtimeOnline` from `lib/chat-context.tsx` to delete ~10 LOC of duplicated state.

- **Add a `topic` prop to `RealtimeStatusPill`** so callers can scope the offline indicator to a single channel (chat inbox, marketplace listings) instead of the aggregate `connectionState`. The pill currently shows "offline" when *any* tracked topic is `connecting`, which can flash a misleading state on the marketplace screen while the chat channel reconnects. `isTopicOnline(topic)` is already exposed on the context — `<RealtimeStatusPill topic="marketplace-listings-inserts" />` would be a one-line addition that derives a per-topic pill state.

- **Render a global "reconnecting" banner in `app/_layout.tsx`** — the registry now publishes connection state app-wide, but only `app/marketplace.tsx` shows the pill. A one-line `<RealtimeStatusPill />` in `_layout.tsx`'s `AppShell` (between `<NavigationBreadcrumbs />` and `<Stack>`) would surface socket loss on every screen, matching how mainstream chat apps render a persistent "Connecting…" header instead of per-screen indicators.

- **Add a `useTopicOnline(topic)` convenience hook** to `lib/realtime-status-context.tsx`. Today consumers must call `useRealtimeStatus().isTopicOnline(topic)`, which re-renders on every snapshot change even if the specific topic's state didn't move. A `useTopicOnline(topic)` hook backed by `useSyncExternalStore` (or a memoized selector) would only re-render on the *topic-specific* transitions — important for `app/chat/[id].tsx` which renders on every keystroke and shouldn't re-render when an unrelated marketplace channel reconnects.

- **Surface the registry snapshot in the diagnostics screen** — `app/diagnostics.tsx` (if it exists, or a future debug route) could render `Array.from(getRegistryStatusSnapshot().entries())` so engineers can see exactly which topics are subscribed/online during a session. Today the only way to inspect realtime state is via the Sentry breadcrumb timeline, which is post-hoc and limited; an in-app view would help triage "why isn't my marketplace updating?" complaints without a remote-debug round-trip.

### Realtime channel fan-out registry (2026-05-21)

- **Migrate `subscribeToTyping` onto the fan-out registry too** — today it's the one remaining inline `client.channel(topic)` consumer in `lib/supabase-chat.ts`. The presence semantics (`.track({ typing })` + per-user state) don't fit the current `configure(channel, emit)` API, but extending `subscribeShared` with an optional `presence?: { selfPayload, onStateChange }` block would let the typing channel share the same ref-counting + status fan-out as inbox/listings, keeping the "one socket per app" invariant from regressing when the same chat is open in two tabs of the same realm.

- **Move the realtime connection-state pill into a `RealtimeStatusProvider` consuming `subscribeShared`** — the next `.tasks.md` suggestion (line 58, "Track the RealtimeClient connection state … on a shared context value") is now a one-line plumbing job. Have the provider call `subscribeShared` with a sentinel topic + a no-op configurator just to register a status handler; the registry's late-joiner replay means every screen reads the live status without each module wiring its own listener.

- **Auto-fan-out `closeSharedRealtimeClient` into the registry** — today `closeSharedRealtimeClient` clears the module-scope cache in `lib/supabase-realtime.ts` but the registry's `WeakMap<RealtimeClient, …>` entries for the closed client still hold references to dead channels until GC. A `__resetRegistryFor(client)` helper called from `closeSharedRealtimeClient` would drop the per-client map deterministically + tear down any subscribed channels' fan-out handlers so a sign-out + re-sign-in cycle starts clean.

- **Add a structural test asserting no `app/**/*.tsx` calls `client.channel(...)` directly** — the registry is now the canonical entry point for new realtime consumers, but nothing prevents a future screen from re-introducing the inline-channel pattern. A regex grep across `app/**` + `components/**` paired with an allowlist for the registry itself would catch the regression in CI before it ships.

- **Promote the per-handler `try/catch` isolation contract into a typed `FanOut<T>` helper** — the registry hand-rolls the "for (handler of set) { try { handler() } catch {} }" loop in both the payload and status paths. Lifting it into a tiny `createFanOut<T>(): { add, remove, emit }` helper in `lib/fan-out.ts` would let the next telemetry stream (PostHog session events? Sentry breadcrumbs?) reuse the same isolation guarantee with one import.

### useNow hook (2026-05-21)

- **Wire `useNow()` into `app/chats.tsx`** — the chat list is the highest-value consumer. Today every preview's "X minutes ago" is frozen at last context re-render; subscribing the list (or each row) to `useNow()` makes the label live with negligible cost now that `formatRelativeDate` is memoised.

- **Wire `useNow()` into `app/listing/[id].tsx`** — both the "Listed X ago" header and each price-history entry's relative date benefit. The screen already imports `formatRelativeDate`; threading `useNow()` through `t("marketplaceListedAt", { when: formatRelativeDate(listing.createdAt) })` is a one-line change once the hook lands.

- **Singleton ticker via `useSyncExternalStore`** — the per-mount `setInterval` pattern is fine for ≤10 screens, but a future dashboard rendering dozens of relative-time labels would carry dozens of independent intervals. A single module-scope ticker exposing a `subscribe(listener)` API consumed via `useSyncExternalStore` would collapse them to one timer with deterministic React tear-off semantics.

- **Pause the ticker on `document.visibilityState === "hidden"`** — a backgrounded web tab doesn't need to re-render relative labels. Pairing the singleton ticker (above) with a `visibilitychange` listener that suspends ticks while the tab is hidden saves real CPU on long-lived sessions.

- **Add a `useTimestampWithTick(iso)` convenience that combines `useNow` + `formatRelativeDate`** — every caller writes the same pair of lines (`const now = useNow(); const label = useMemo(() => formatRelativeDate(iso), [iso, now])`). Promoting that to a single helper would cut each migration call site from 3 lines to 1 and gives a natural place to add per-locale memoization later.

### formatRelativeDate memoization (2026-05-21)

- **Extend the cache to `Intl.NumberFormat` / `Intl.DateTimeFormat`** — `lib/locale-helpers.ts` already exports `getDefaultLocaleForLanguage`; pairing it with a `getNumberFormat(bcp47, opts)` + `getDateTimeFormat(bcp47, opts)` helper following the same Map-cache pattern would close the same allocation hot-path for currency/price formatting in `<CurrencyInput>` and `app/listing/[id].tsx`.

- **Add a benchmark in `__tests__/format-relative-date-memoization.test.ts`** — assert that 1000 calls with the same locale return in under, say, 5ms (where unmemoized was ~50ms). A timing-based assertion would catch a future refactor accidentally reintroducing `new Intl.RelativeTimeFormat` inside the function body, even if the cache map declaration is preserved.

- **Auto-tick relative timestamps via a shared `useNow()` hook** — the existing suggestion in `.tasks.md` (line 76) becomes much cheaper now that the formatter is cached: re-rendering "1 minute ago" → "2 minutes ago" every 60s no longer re-walks the ICU tables. A 30-line hook in `lib/use-now.ts` paired with the new cache makes the auto-tick negligible-cost.

- **Promote `getRelativeTimeFormat` out of `i18n-context.tsx`** — the formatter cache is locale-derived, not React-context-derived; it belongs next to `getDefaultLocaleForLanguage` in `lib/locale-helpers.ts` so non-React call sites (server-side rendering, build-time string generation) can use the same primitive without bringing in the i18n provider.

- **Add an LRU bound to the cache** — today the Map is unbounded. Six locales today, fine; a future "all 24 EU languages" launch would let it grow to 24 entries (still cheap), but a strict LRU eviction (e.g. cap=32) is a one-line `if (cache.size > 32) cache.delete(cache.keys().next().value)` guard that future-proofs the pattern.

### closeSharedRealtimeClient on sign-out (2026-05-21)

- **Call `closeSharedRealtimeClient` from the `SIGNED_OUT` branch of `onAuthStateChange` too** — today the cleanup runs only on the user-initiated `signOut`/`deleteAccount` paths. If a session is invalidated server-side (admin revoke, password reset, expired refresh) the socket would stay open until the next reload. Mirroring the cleanup inside the auth-state listener catches every termination path.

- **Drain pending channel state from each context before disconnect** — `lib/supabase-chat.ts` and `lib/supabase-marketplace.ts` hold per-screen channels off the shared client. `closeSharedRealtimeClient` just calls `disconnect()`, which leaves the per-context `channelRef`s pointing at dead channels until those screens re-subscribe. Exposing a `closeAllSharedChannels()` that walks `client.getChannels()` would close the loop deterministically.

- **Reset the realtime cache in `clearRuntimeSupabaseConfig` too** — the URL/key reset path constructs new credentials but leaves the cached `sharedRealtimeClient` pointing at the OLD endpoint. A user who switches projects via the runtime config form would silently keep the socket alive against the old URL until something else nukes it. The new helper makes this a one-line fix.

- **Expose `getSharedRealtimeClientState()` for diagnostics** — diagnose stale sockets post-disconnect by exposing the connection state (CONNECTING/OPEN/CLOSED) of the cached client. Pairs naturally with the future "reconnecting" pill suggestion in `.tasks.md` and gives QA a one-tap visibility point.

- **Add a `disconnect-on-window-blur` heuristic** — release the socket when the web tab is hidden for >5 minutes (`document.visibilityState`). Useful for users who pin the app in a background tab — keeps the connection count under Supabase's free-tier WebSocket limit without forcing sign-out.

### Test bootstrap (2026-05-21)

- **Migrate `__resetSentryForTests` / `__resetAnalyticsForTests` into the same global bootstrap** — both helpers are currently re-called inside every Sentry/Analytics test file's `beforeEach`. Moving them into `__tests__/test-globals.ts` (with the same `require.cache` lazy-peek pattern that supabase-realtime uses) would shrink each suite by ~3 lines and close the same cross-test contamination footgun globally instead of per-file.

- **Auto-register module-resets via a `registerTestReset(fn)` side-channel** — instead of the bootstrap hand-maintaining a list of `require.cache` paths to peek at, expose a `registerTestReset` in a tiny `lib/test-reset-registry.ts` that any module can call from its top level. The bootstrap then iterates registered fns; no path strings, no growing list of `path.join(...)` calls. Mirrors how `expo-router`'s `Stack.Screen` self-registers without the parent maintaining a child list.

- **Add a `--watch` mode to the test script** that re-runs only affected suites on change (`tsx --import ./__tests__/test-globals.ts --test --watch __tests__/*.test.ts`). With the preload now in place, watch mode would re-apply the global beforeEach automatically — fast inner loop for the multi-second full-suite run.

- **Wire the test-globals preload into the lint:ci alias** — today `lint:ci` already runs `tsc --noEmit && npm test`, so it inherits the preload via `npm test`. But future contributors may add a separate "fast" test script that forgets `--import`. Add a structural test that asserts every package.json `*test*` script that runs `tsx --test` also carries `--import ./__tests__/test-globals.ts`.

- **Capture the realtime cache state in a debug snapshot** — the bootstrap silently resets; if a test fails after a contamination round-trip, there's nothing in the failure output linking the cause to the cache. Logging `[test-globals] reset shared realtime client` when `DEBUG_TEST_GLOBALS=1` would make it trivial to see whether the cache *was* populated when the failing test ran — useful when chasing flaky integration tests.

### i18n ↔ locale parity (2026-05-21)

- **Export `languageOptions` from `lib/i18n-context.tsx`** — the parity test currently parses the array from the source string via regex because `languageOptions` is module-local. Promoting it to a named export (it's already part of the public `I18nContextValue` shape returned by `useI18n`) would let the test import the actual array and remove the regex parse, closing the small risk that a future refactor changes the literal shape and slips past the regex.

- **Extend parity to translations record keys** — the test catches drift between `languageOptions` and the locale maps but not between the picker and the `translations` record (`{ en, ru, be, pl, de, es }`). A future language added to the picker without a translation map would render bare keys; mirror the same parity assertion against the `translations` Record<AppLanguage, TranslationMap> declaration.

- **Pull the EXPECTED_LANGUAGES list into a shared `__tests__/helpers/supported-languages.ts`** — both `i18n-translations.test.ts` and the new parity test hand-maintain the list of language codes. A single tuple consumed by both keeps them in lockstep and is the natural place to add the next language.

- **Make `languageOptions` order-stable via an `as const` tuple typed against `AppLanguage`** — today the array is loosely typed `{ code: AppLanguage; label: string }[]`. Switching to `as const satisfies readonly { code: AppLanguage; label: string }[]` lifts the codes into a literal union, lets the i18n type system flag a code that isn't a known `AppLanguage`, and makes the picker ordering visible to consumers.

- **Add a runtime guard `assertLanguageMapsAligned()` in `lib/locale-helpers.ts`** — invoked once at module init in dev (`__DEV__`), `console.warn`s when `languageCurrencyMap` and `languageLocaleMap` cover different key sets. The new test guards drift at PR time; a runtime guard closes the gap if someone bypasses the test via an env override (the maps are env-merged for `LANGUAGE_CURRENCY`).

### User preferred currency (2026-05-20)

- **Surface the preferred currency on the settings screen** — add a "Default currency" row next to the language picker so a power user can change it from one place instead of editing a draft listing. The `getUserPreferredCurrency` / `setUserPreferredCurrency` pair is already in place; the UI is the only missing piece.

- **Reactive subscription via a `useUserPreferredCurrency()` hook** — every screen currently hydrates the value with a one-shot `useEffect`. A tiny in-module subscriber registry inside `locale-helpers.ts` (set-on-write fans out to listeners) would keep multiple open forms in sync without each one polling AsyncStorage.

- **Server-side sync for cross-device parity** — persist the preferred currency into `profiles.preferred_currency text` and read it back on auth so a user who picks JPY on the web sees JPY on iOS without re-picking. Today the slot is local-only; a `chat_id_integrity`-style migration plus a small `lib/supabase-profiles.ts` field would close the gap.

- **Show a "currency changed" toast on first persist** — non-obvious side effect (the next listing form will remember the pick) currently happens silently. A one-shot toast keyed on the first `setUserPreferredCurrency` call this session would teach users the feature exists.

- **Migrate to the same env-override pattern as `EXPO_PUBLIC_LANGUAGE_CURRENCY`** — add `EXPO_PUBLIC_PREFERRED_CURRENCY_DEFAULT` that ships a build-time override (e.g. JPY for the JP App Store track) honoured only when no per-user pick has been stored yet. Mirrors how `parseLanguageCurrencyOverride` already lets QA flip per-region defaults without a code change.

### Chat DB (2026-05-16)

- **Cursor pagination for `fetchMessagesForChat`** — it currently `select=*&order=created_at.asc` with no `limit`, so a long-lived conversation pulls the entire history into memory on every hydrate. Add `&limit=50` + a `created_at` cursor (or PostgREST `Range` header) and load older pages on scroll-up. Bounds memory and free-tier egress.

- **Realtime reconnect backfill** — while the WebSocket is down, `subscribeToInbox` misses INSERTs and only `refreshFromCloud` (mount-time) closes the gap. On `SUBSCRIBED` after a drop, fetch messages `created_at=gt.<last-known>` per active chat so no message is silently lost during a flaky connection.

- **First-class conversations table** — replace the free-text `chat_id` with a `conversations(id uuid, user_a uuid, user_b uuid, UNIQUE(user_a,user_b))` table and a `chat_messages.conversation_id uuid REFERENCES conversations(id)`. A real FK + unique participant pair is stronger than the derived-string CHECK and unlocks per-conversation metadata (muted, archived, last_message_at) without re-deriving from messages.

- **Functional idempotency test with a mocked fetcher** — the new ignore-duplicates path is only covered structurally. Add a `__tests__/supabase-chat-idempotency.test.ts` that injects a fake `fetcher` returning `200 []` and asserts `sendMessage` resolves to the synthesized message (not `null`), plus a fake returning a populated row for the happy path.

- **`chat_messages.client_id` + server uuid split** — keep the server `id uuid DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()` authoritative and add a separate indexed `client_id uuid` (the composition-time key) with a UNIQUE constraint for idempotency. Decouples "who owns the primary key" from "idempotency key", which is the canonical chat-storage pattern and avoids ever trusting a client-supplied PK.

- **SPA fallback regression guard** — Add a CI step that runs `npm run build` then asserts (a) `dist/404.html` contains `location.replace`, (b) `dist/index.html` contains `data-spa-restore`. This catches a future contributor accidentally reverting the post-build script (e.g. swapping back to `cp dist/index.html dist/404.html`) before the change reaches production iOS users.

- **Service worker for instant deep-link load** — Even with the sessionStorage redirect, the user sees a flash of the redirect page on iPhone. Registering a service worker (Workbox `NetworkFirst` + `NavigationFallback` to `/collectables/index.html`) would let cached deep links resolve to 200 directly and remove the redirect entirely on repeat visits.

- **Sentry breadcrumb for SPA URL restore** — Drop an `addBreadcrumb("spa-redirect", { from, to })` inside the restore script (gated on `__sentry_loaded__`) so Sentry sessions show exactly which deep-link URLs hit the 404 fallback. Useful for ranking which routes deserve a real static export.

- **Static export of common collection IDs** — Expo Router could pre-render the top-N most-shared collections at build time (e.g. by reading from Supabase) so their URLs return real 200s without the redirect dance. Reduces flicker and helps SEO for public collections.

- **Migrate baseUrl to a single source** — `app.json` declares `expo.experiments.baseUrl`, `lib/url-helpers.ts` infers it at runtime, and `scripts/build-spa-fallback.ts` re-reads it from app.json. A single `lib/base-url.ts` exporting a const + a helper that all three import would eliminate the drift risk if the deployment path ever changes (e.g. moving off the `1337ninja1337.github.io/collectables` prefix).

- **CI guard: regenerate the .pbit and fail on drift** — Add a `build:powerbi` step to the GitHub Actions workflow that runs `npm run build:powerbi` then `git diff --exit-code docs/powerbi/Collectables-Starter.pbit`. The `powerbi-template.test.ts` parity test already catches drift, but a workflow step makes the regeneration command discoverable and stops a stale binary ever reaching `main` if someone edits `measures.dax`/`queries.m` without rebuilding.

- **Reference report layout in the .pbit** — The template currently opens to a blank canvas. Build a real `Report/Layout` with a line chart (`occurred_at` × `DAU`), two KPI cards (`ListingFunnelRate`, `PremiumConversionRate7d`), and a default theme resource package so users get a dashboard on first open. Gate it behind a `--with-report` flag so the minimal (lower open-risk) layout stays the default until it's validated in Power BI Desktop.

- **Generalise the OPC/ZIP writer** — `zipStore`/`readZipEntries`/`crc32` in `lib/powerbi-template.ts` are a generic, dependency-free deterministic ZIP. Promote them to `lib/opc-zip.ts` so future binary artefacts (e.g. an `.xlsx` data export, a bundled theme pack) reuse the same byte-stable packer instead of pulling in `jszip`/`archiver`.

- **Power BI parameter validation in the M** — The four `Supabase*` parameters are free-text. Add a guard in the partition M (`if SupabasePort = "" then error "SupabasePort is required" else ...`) and a regex check on the host so a user who clicks through the prompt with blanks gets a clear Power Query error instead of an opaque PostgreSQL connection failure.

- **`.pbit` schema-version matrix doc** — `compatibilityLevel: 1550` targets a broad Power BI range, but the report/model JSON evolves across Desktop releases. Add a short table in `docs/powerbi/README.md` mapping the Power BI Desktop versions the template was sanity-checked against (and known-incompatible ones) so users hitting an open failure immediately know to fall back to the copy-paste assets.

- **pgTAP automated RLS test** — The Analytics #16 leak check is a manual paste-into-SQL-editor checklist. Add a `supabase/tests/analytics_events_rls.sql` pgTAP test (`SET ROLE anon; SELECT throws_ok('SELECT … analytics_events', '42501')`) so `supabase test db` enforces the default-deny posture in CI instead of relying on an operator remembering to run it.

- **Reusable RLS-deny audit query** — Generalise the leak check into a single query over `pg_policies` + `information_schema.role_table_grants` that lists every `public.*` table reachable by `anon`/`authenticated`, and document it in MANUAL-TASKS.md. One run flags *any* table that regresses to readable, not just `analytics_events` — cheap defence-in-depth as more tables land.

- **CI grep guard against analytics_events policies** — Add a lint/CI step that greps `supabase/migrations/*.sql` for `CREATE POLICY .* analytics_events` (executable SQL, comment-stripped) and fails the build. The structural test already asserts this for the one migration; a directory-wide grep catches a *future* migration file that adds a permissive policy from outside `20260508_*`.

- **Edge Function service-role assertion** — `analytics-mirror` inserts with the service-role key; add a startup self-check (and a unit assertion) that the resolved key is the service-role JWT (`role: "service_role"` claim) and not the anon key, so a misconfigured secret fails loudly at deploy time instead of silently 401/permission-denying every insert against the RLS'd table.

- **Retention / PII sweep for analytics_events** — The store is long-tail by design; add a documented `DELETE FROM analytics_events WHERE occurred_at < now() - interval '13 months'` cron (pg_cron) plus a note in the privacy doc, so the unbounded event history honours a stated retention window for GDPR — pairs naturally with the existing default-deny posture.

### Analytics rate limiter (2026-05-19)

- **Surface a dropped-event counter** — `rateLimitAllow()` silently returns false when the window is full, so an over-firing screen looks identical to a quiet one. Track a module-level `droppedEventCount` and a `getAnalyticsRateLimitStatus()` snapshot (mirrors `getSentryStatus()`); a future admin/devtools probe can then tell "no events" apart from "rate-limited", which is the difference between a dead instrumentation path and a hot loop.

- **Per-event-name sub-limits** — A single global 200/min bucket lets one chatty event (e.g. a mis-placed `item_photo_attached` in a render) starve rare high-value events like `premium_activated`. A small `Map<AnalyticsEventName, number[]>` with a low per-name cap (e.g. 30/min) plus the existing global ceiling would protect conversion-critical events from a noisy neighbour.

- **Coalesce dropped events into one summary capture** — Instead of fully discarding everything past the cap, emit a single `analytics_rate_limited` event once per window carrying `{ dropped, topEventName }`. Keeps the free-tier bounded while preserving the signal that *something* is looping — currently the loop is invisible in PostHog itself.

- **Shared rate-limiter primitive** — `lib/sentry.ts` and `lib/analytics.ts` now carry byte-identical `RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MS` / `recentEvents` / `rateLimitAllow` blocks. Extract a `createSlidingWindowLimiter(max, windowMs)` factory into `lib/rate-limit.ts` (returning `{ allow, reset }`) so both wrappers, plus future ones (chat send, marketplace claim), share one tested implementation instead of three copies drifting apart.

- **Make the cap env-tunable** — Add `EXPO_PUBLIC_ANALYTICS_MAX_EVENTS_PER_MIN` resolved via the proposed `resolveNumericEnv` helper so incident response can throttle analytics to near-zero (or raise it for a load test) without a redeploy — same operational lever the `EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED` kill-switch suggestion proposes for WebSockets.

### Diagnostics Do-Not-Track (2026-05-19)

- **Surface a "respecting your browser's Do-Not-Track" line in settings** — When `readDoNotTrack()` is true and the user has made no explicit choice, the toggle silently sits OFF with no explanation. Add an i18n hint under the toggle (`t("diagnosticsDntHint")`) shown only in that state so an EU user understands *why* it defaulted off and that flipping it on is an explicit consent override — clearer GDPR UX and removes a "why is this off?" support question.

- **Global Privacy Control (GPC) signal** — GPC (`navigator.globalPrivacyControl === true`) is the modern successor to DNT and is legally recognised under CCPA/CPRA. Extend `readDoNotTrack()` (or add a sibling `readPrivacySignal()`) to also honour GPC so the opt-out default tracks the standard regulators now point to, not just the deprecated DNT header.

- **Re-evaluate DNT default on web focus** — DNT is only read once on provider mount. If a user changes their browser DNT setting mid-session (or in another tab) the app keeps the stale default until reload. A `visibilitychange`/`focus` listener (web-only) that re-runs `resolveDiagnosticsEnabled` when there's still no explicit stored choice would keep the signal honoured live.

- **Persist a `source` alongside the stored choice** — `{ enabled }` doesn't record whether the value came from an explicit user toggle, a DNT default, or a migration. Storing `{ enabled, source: "user" | "dnt-default" }` lets a future migration safely re-derive defaults (e.g. if the DNT policy changes) without clobbering real user consent, and feeds an analytics property on how many installs are DNT-defaulted.

- **`__tests__/diagnostics-provider-wiring.test.ts`** — The pure helpers are well covered but the `DiagnosticsProvider` effect (hydrate → `setSentryOptOut`/`setAnalyticsOptOut`/`setClarityOptOut` + conditional `init*`) is only exercised indirectly. Add a structural test asserting the provider calls `resolveDiagnosticsEnabled(raw, readDoNotTrack())` on hydrate and that `setDiagnosticsEnabled(false)` calls all three `shutdown*` paths — guards the GDPR contract against a refactor that drops a sub-processor from the fan-out.

### Privacy policy & sub-processors (2026-05-19)

- **Generate PRIVACY.md from the App Privacy table** — `APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md` §6 now holds the canonical table + sub-processor paragraphs, but the actual public `PRIVACY.md` (the URL App Review checks) is described, not generated. Add a `scripts/build-privacy-md.ts` that extracts the table + paragraphs into a standalone `PRIVACY.md` deployed to GitHub Pages, plus a parity test, so the published policy can never drift from the App Store Connect declaration.

- **Localise the public privacy paragraphs** — The app ships 6 languages (`ru/en/be/pl/de/es`) but the privacy paragraphs are English-only. EU (GDPR) and Apple guidelines expect the policy in the app's supported languages; wire the paragraphs through the existing `t()` i18n catalogue (or a `docs/privacy/<lang>.md` set) so a German/Polish user gets a policy they can read.

- **CI guard: SDK ↔ privacy-table parity** — Add a test that greps `package.json` + `lib/clarity.ts` for telemetry SDKs (`@sentry/*`, `posthog-react-native`, `clarity.ms`) and asserts each has a matching row in the `APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md` App Privacy table. Today adding a new analytics SDK wouldn't fail any check until App Review rejects the build — a parity test shifts that left.

- **Document the PostHog/Clarity data-retention windows** — The Sentry paragraph states a concrete 90-day retention; the new PostHog and Clarity paragraphs don't. GDPR Art. 13(2)(a) requires the storage period. Add the configured/contractual retention for each (PostHog project setting, Clarity's 30-day default) so the disclosure is complete.

- **Surface the active sub-processor list in-app** — Add a read-only "Data & privacy" sub-screen under Settings that renders the same sub-processor list (Sentry/PostHog/Clarity) and a link to the policy. Several App Review rejections stem from the policy being hard to reach; an in-app surface that mirrors `APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md` closes that and gives users one place to see who processes their data.

### Analytics test-coverage audit (2026-05-19)

- **Functional rate-limiter window-expiry test** — `analytics-rate-limit.test.ts` covers the cap and the reset helper but not the *sliding* behaviour. Inject a `now` clock (or temporarily monkeypatch `Date.now`) and assert that events allowed >60s ago no longer count, so a regression that turns the sliding window into a fixed one (or drops the `recentEvents.filter` cutoff) is caught.

- **CI guard: every test file is actually picked up by the glob** — `npm test` runs `tsx --test __tests__/*.test.ts`; a file mis-named `*.tests.ts` or in a sub-dir is silently skipped (it would still pass CI). Add a meta-test that globs `__tests__/**` and asserts every `*.test.ts` it finds is also matched by the exact `__tests__/*.test.ts` pattern the script uses.

- **Assert AnalyticsProvider mounts under DiagnosticsProvider** — wiring tests check AnalyticsProvider sits under Auth/I18n/Premium, but not that it mounts *inside* `<DiagnosticsProvider>`. If it ever rendered outside, `identifyUser` could fire before the opt-out flag hydrates. A one-line index-order assertion closes that ordering gap.

- **Snapshot the `AnalyticsEventName` ↔ `ANALYTICS_EVENTS` parity at the type level** — `analytics-events.test.ts` checks the runtime keys equal the expected list, but a `satisfies Record<AnalyticsEventName, AnalyticsEventDefinition>` annotation on `ANALYTICS_EVENTS` would make a missing/extra event a *compile* error too, catching drift before the test even runs.

- **Coverage threshold in CI** — There's no coverage gate, so a new uncovered branch can land green. Wire `node --test --experimental-test-coverage` (or `c8`) with a modest line/branch floor on `lib/analytics*.ts` + `lib/diagnostics-context.tsx` so the telemetry/consent core can't silently lose coverage.

- **Make `resolveNumericEnv` behaviourally unit-testable** — it now lives in `lib/env.ts` which imports `react-native` (`Platform`), so it can only be structurally tested. Move the pure parser into the existing react-native-free `lib/url-helpers.ts` (or a new `lib/env-helpers.ts`) and re-export it from `lib/env.ts`, mirroring the `getAppBaseUrl` → `resolveAppBaseUrl` split. Then a real `__tests__/env-helpers.test.ts` can assert the empty/NaN/zero/negative/valid matrix instead of regex-matching source.

- **Add an optional `{ min, max }` clamp to `resolveNumericEnv`** — the `EXPO_PUBLIC_PROFILE_CACHE_TTL_MS < 30s` foot-gun already has its own pending task (a warning toast). A `resolveNumericEnv(raw, def, { min: 30_000 })` overload that floors out-of-range overrides at the source would protect Supabase free-tier limits for *every* future tunable (chat poll, marketplace cache) without each caller re-deriving the guard.

- **Promote `normaliseEnvironment` into `lib/env.ts` next to `resolveNumericEnv`** — `lib/sentry-config.ts` / `lib/analytics-config.ts` both re-implement an env-name normaliser; co-locating it with the new numeric resolver finishes the "one env-parse surface" consolidation the `.tasks` entry started and lets a single `runtime-config-parity` test cover both.

- **Lint guard against computed `process.env[...]` access** — the Metro-inlining foot-gun is currently policed by hand-written structural tests (`sentry-env-inlining`, `env-resolve-numeric`). A 15-line ESLint `no-restricted-syntax` rule banning `MemberExpression[computed=true][object.object.name="process"][object.property.name="env"]` would enforce it codebase-wide and fail the PR instead of one specific file's test.

- **Reuse `resolveNumericEnv` for the next tunable now, not later** — the `.tasks` entry cites "chat poll interval, marketplace cache" as future beneficiaries but ships zero second callers, so the helper's generality is unverified. Migrate one real numeric knob (e.g. a `EXPO_PUBLIC_CHAT_POLL_MS` for `lib/chat-context.tsx`) in the same PR family so the abstraction is proven by a second consumer rather than asserted.

### Low-TTL warning toast (2026-05-20)

- **Surface the configured TTL value inside the warning toast** — today the message reads "below 30 seconds" without echoing what the operator actually set. Threading the parsed milliseconds via `t("profileCacheTtlLowMessage", { configured, minimum })` would make the warning self-diagnosing ("you set 5000ms, recommended ≥30000ms") and remove the operator's "what did I set, again?" round-trip to `.env`.

- **Promote `lowProfileCacheTtlWarningShown` into a typed `lib/once-toast.ts` registry** — the module-scope `let warned = false` pattern is now used by Sentry (`__resetSentryForTests`), Analytics (`__resetAnalyticsRateLimitForTests`) and this new TTL warning. A `registerOnceToast(key, () => …)` helper that owns the flag + reset would shrink each call site to a single `useOnceToast("low-profile-cache-ttl", …)` and centralise the testing escape hatch.

- **Mirror the same soft-floor warning for future TTL overrides** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED` (pending), a hypothetical `EXPO_PUBLIC_CHAT_POLL_MS`, and the marketplace cache TTL all want the same "value below recommended floor → warn once" treatment. A generic `useNumericEnvFloorWarning(rawValue, { minimum, title, message })` hook would let new tunables ship the warning with one line instead of replicating the `useEffect` + module flag in every provider.

- **Document the soft floor in `README-DEPLOY.md` and the upcoming `.env.example`** — the `MINIMUM_RECOMMENDED_PROFILE_CACHE_TTL_MS = 30_000` constant is now the canonical floor but only this file mentions it. Surfacing it in the operator docs (alongside the existing pending "document the env var" suggestion) closes the loop between the warning toast and the place an engineer reads to learn *why* 30s was chosen.

- **Add an `__tests__/i18n-translations-profile-cache.test.ts` parity test** — five language maps now carry `profileCacheTtlLow{Title,Message}`. A structural test that walks every `AppLanguage` and asserts both keys resolve to a non-empty string would catch a future language addition that forgets the override (today `...en` masks the regression at runtime by silently shipping English to a non-English user).

### Tracked `.env.example` + env-doc parity (2026-05-20)

- **Promote the README/.env.example parity scan into a runnable script** — the new `profile-cache-ttl-env-docs.test.ts` walks the README table and asserts every `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` row exists in `.env.example`. Lift the walker into a small `scripts/check-env-docs.ts` so a contributor can run `npm run check:env-docs` locally before pushing, instead of waiting for CI. Pairs naturally with the pending `runtime-config-parity.test.ts` suggestion.

- **Extend the parity test to scan `eas.json` and `.github/workflows/deploy.yml`** — today the scan covers README ⇄ `.env.example` only. The same `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` names also live in EAS secrets and the GitHub Actions secrets block; a four-way scan would catch the "added a new env var to one workflow but missed another" foot-gun that the existing `eas-secrets-parity` suggestion in `.tasks.md` already flagged but never landed.

- **Document `EXPO_PUBLIC_PROFILE_CACHE_TTL_MS` in `APPSTORE-SUBMISSION.md` §13 EAS secrets** — the iOS submission checklist already lists every other `EXPO_PUBLIC_*` as an `eas secret:create …` line; threading the new variable in keeps the iOS build path aligned with the web build path. Today only the web `README-DEPLOY.md` mentions it.

- **Add an `# How to use` header block at the top of `.env.example`** — the file now boots the convention but reads as a flat list. A short stanza pointing at `README-DEPLOY.md` for full descriptions + flagging which vars are optional vs required would shorten an engineer's first-touch from "read three files" to "copy and edit one".

- **Wire `.env.example` placeholders through a structural test that rejects committed `.env`** — the no-secret-in-example guard already exists in the new docs test. Add a counterpart `__tests__/dotenv-not-committed.test.ts` that asserts `.env` is absent from `git ls-files`, so a future contributor running `git add -A` after editing their local `.env` can't accidentally land credentials in a PR.

### Realtime kill-switch (2026-05-20)

- **Surface the kill-switch state on `app/settings.tsx` diagnostics screen** — `EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED=1` silently flips every realtime feature off; a "Realtime: disabled by environment" row (read from `isRealtimeDisabledByEnv(process.env.EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED)`) tells a tester why their chat inbox is offline without spelunking the bundle. Mirrors the pending `getAnalyticsStatus()` diagnostics row suggestion.

- **Add a `closeSharedRealtimeClient()` cleanup that the kill-switch can call** — today flipping the env var on a running session still leaks the active WebSocket because `sharedRealtimeClient` was already constructed. Pairing the kill-switch with a `closeSharedRealtimeClient()` helper (callable from a DevMenu entry or on auth sign-out) would drop the socket promptly. Already pending as its own suggestion — promote both together for incident-response symmetry.

- **Mirror the truthy-literal parser in a shared `lib/env.ts:isTruthyEnv(rawValue)` helper** — the new `isRealtimeDisabledByEnv` accepts `1`/`true`/`yes`. Future boolean toggles (analytics mirror disable, premium-gate bypass, etc.) want the same shape. A 6-line helper next to `resolveNumericEnv` would centralise the lowercase/trim/whitelist dance and let `isRealtimeDisabledByEnv` shrink to a one-liner wrapper.

- **Wire a Sentry breadcrumb when the kill-switch is active** — an `addBreadcrumb("realtime-disabled-by-env", { source: "EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED" })` on first call to `getSharedRealtimeClient()` while disabled would make "user says chat is offline" tickets one grep away in the Sentry timeline. Cheap to add: gated on `__sentry_loaded__` so it no-ops when Sentry isn't configured.

- **Add a runtime integration test for the kill-switch path** — today only structural assertions exist. A test that monkey-patches the env, re-imports the module (via `vm.SourceTextModule` or by exporting a `__buildSharedClient(env)` factory) and asserts `getSharedRealtimeClient()` returns null even when `isSupabaseConfigured` is true would catch a future refactor that re-orders the gates wrong.

### CURRENCY_CHIPS picker whitelist (2026-05-20)

- **Tighten `<CurrencyInput>`'s currency prop type from `string` to `CurrencyChipCode`** — the new literal-union type is exported but not yet threaded through the component props. Switching `currency: string` → `currency: CurrencyChipCode` makes a typo on any consumer page (`<CurrencyInput currency="USDT" />` → arbitrary unknown chip) fail at compile time instead of silently rendering nothing-selected. Same for `onChangeCurrency: (c: string) => void`.

- **Reuse `CURRENCY_CHIPS` in `app/create.tsx`'s autocomplete to short-list the most common codes** — today the full 150-entry `lib/currencies.ts` dictionary feeds the autocomplete; surfacing `CURRENCY_CHIPS` as a "Common" header pinned to the top of the suggestions would speed up the 99% case (USD/EUR/GBP/etc.) without removing the long tail. The two lists are intentionally separate; a UI that uses both gets the best of each.

- **Add an `EXPO_PUBLIC_EXTRA_CURRENCY_CHIPS=NZD,SGD` operator override** — `CURRENCY_CHIPS` is now centralised but still hard-coded. A comma-separated env var read once at module load (using the same literal-`process.env.X` pattern as `EXPO_PUBLIC_REALTIME_DISABLED`) would let a regional launch add chips without a code change. Mirror the validation: filter inputs against `lib/currencies.ts:isCurrencyCode` so a typo doesn't render a broken chip.

- **Promote a `localeDisplayName(code, language)` helper next to `CURRENCY_CHIPS`** — today the picker renders raw codes ("USD", "EUR"). `Intl.DisplayNames` makes `"USD"` → `"US Dollar"` (English) / `"Доллар США"` (Russian) trivial; co-locating the helper in `lib/locale-helpers.ts` keeps the picker presentation logic near its data and lines up with the pending `getDefaultLocaleForLanguage` suggestion.

- **Add a `__tests__/currency-chips-iso-4217-parity.test.ts` that asserts every entry in `CURRENCY_CHIPS` exists in `lib/currencies.ts:CURRENCIES`** — a future contributor adding a deprecated currency code (e.g. ISO 4217 retired some after 2024) to the chips list would render a chip that the autocomplete can't validate. A 10-line parity test catches the drift between the curated shortlist and the canonical dictionary.

### BCP-47 locale helper (2026-05-20)

- **Use `getDefaultLocaleForLanguage` to drive a centralised `formatCurrency(amount, currency, language)` helper** — today `<CurrencyInput>` shows the raw code (e.g. `USD 12.34`); pairing the new BCP-47 lookup with `new Intl.NumberFormat(locale, { style: "currency", currency })` would render `$12.34` / `12,34 €` / `12,34 zł` automatically. A 10-line helper in `lib/locale-helpers.ts` would replace every hand-rolled price label across `listing/[id]`, `chats`, marketplace.

- **Extend the parity test to scan `languageOptions` (i18n) against `languageLocaleMap` and `languageCurrencyMap`** — today the new test asserts the two locale-helpers maps share a key set. Adding a third arm — every key in `languageOptions` must also exist in both maps — would close the "new language added to the picker but not to the formatter maps" foot-gun (pending suggestion at line ~52 of `.tasks.md`).

- **Add region-fallback constants** (`DEFAULT_LOCALE = "en-US"`, `DEFAULT_REGION = "US"`) **next to the new map** so a future caller that needs *only* the region (e.g. tax/VAT lookup) doesn't have to `.split("-").pop()` the BCP-47 tag. Cheap encapsulation that grows with the i18n surface.

- **Mirror the new helper inside the chat realtime client** — `lib/chat-context.tsx` formats message timestamps with `formatRelativeDate(iso, language)`. The BCP-47 upgrade is now active there for free, but a future `formatExactTime(iso, language)` would benefit from the same `Intl.DateTimeFormat(getDefaultLocaleForLanguage(language), { hour, minute })` pattern — co-locate the second helper next to the first.

- **Document the new map in `.env.example` as a comment block** so an engineer adding a new language for QA understands they need to touch *three* lib files: `LANGUAGE_LOCALE`, `LANGUAGE_CURRENCY`, and the i18n translations map. Today the trio is a tribal-knowledge requirement.

### Language→currency env override (2026-05-20)

- **Expose a `__resetLanguageCurrencyForTests()` helper** in `lib/locale-helpers.ts` that re-evaluates `parseLanguageCurrencyOverride(process.env.EXPO_PUBLIC_LANGUAGE_CURRENCY)` and rebuilds `LANGUAGE_CURRENCY`. Today the map is captured once at module-load time, so a test that wants to assert real override behaviour (vs. structural-only) has no clean way to set the env var mid-suite and observe the change. Mirrors the `__resetSharedRealtimeClientForTests` / `__resetLowProfileCacheTtlWarningForTests` pattern.

- **Warn once at runtime when `EXPO_PUBLIC_LANGUAGE_CURRENCY` carries dropped tokens** (e.g. `ru:EURO` is silently ignored today). A single `toast.info` listing the rejected entries — gated on `__DEV__` so it doesn't ship to production — would surface typo'd overrides during QA instead of letting the operator wonder why their override "didn't work". Mirrors the low-TTL warning toast pattern shipped on 2026-05-20.

- **Extend the parser to accept fallback-currency syntax** like `ru:RUB|EUR` so QA can stage a primary + fallback currency for A/B testing locale launches. Today the parser is strict 1:1; a `|`-separated tail would unlock a `getDefaultCurrencyCandidatesForLanguage(language): string[]` helper for future fallback-aware pickers without re-implementing the parse-and-validate dance.

- **Add an `EXPO_PUBLIC_LANGUAGE_LOCALE` companion env override** (format `ru:ru-RU,en:en-GB`) in `lib/locale-helpers.ts` mirroring this task's shape, so QA can flip BCP-47 region tags (date/number formatting) per language alongside the currency flip. The two maps already share a key set per the existing parity test — a parallel parser + structural test would close the symmetry gap.

- **Migrate `EXPO_PUBLIC_PROFILE_CACHE_TTL_MS` to use the same defaults-then-override merge pattern this task introduced** — promote a `DEFAULT_PROFILE_CACHE_TTL_MS = 600_000` next to the resolver in `lib/env.ts` (already exists locally in `lib/social-context.tsx` as `DEFAULT_VIEWER_PROFILE_TTL_MS`) and export it so a future test or operator UI can show "configured: X (default: Y)" without re-declaring the constant. Cheap consolidation that mirrors the new `DEFAULT_LANGUAGE_CURRENCY` export shape.

### TAG_* categorical palette (2026-05-23)

- **Export the `TAG_COLORS` rotation array from `lib/design-tokens.ts` itself** so the categorical palette ships as a first-class token-module export (`export const TAG_COLORS = [AMBER_ACCENT, TAG_RUST, ...]`) and the create-item screen consumes the same array a future settings/profile screen would. Today `TAG_COLORS` is re-declared at the top of `app/create.tsx` — DRY-ing it into the design-tokens module would also let the existing palette-frozen test in `__tests__/design-tokens.test.ts` enforce the rotation order (so a tag re-shuffling fails CI). Sub-payoff: any future `TagColorPicker` component can `import { TAG_COLORS } from "@/lib/design-tokens"` without re-implementing the array.

- **Add a `TAG_*` adoption test that asserts no `app/**/*.tsx` file re-declares a literal `["#d89c5b", "#c47a5a", ...]` array** — the 10-color tag rotation is now a brand-anchored palette; a future contributor copy-pasting the array into `app/item/[id].tsx` (next migration target) would silently bypass the centralized palette. A grep-style structural test (`assert.equal(src.match(/"#c47a5a"/g)?.length ?? 0, 0)` across the `app/` tree) closes the regression vector for free.

- **Wire the existing `TAG_COLORS[tags.length % TAG_COLORS.length]` modulo-rotation into a `pickNextTagColor(existing: ItemTag[]): string` pure helper** in `lib/tag-colors.ts` — today the modulo lives inline in two onSubmit handlers (`tagInput`-keyboard-submit + `tagAddButton`-press) in `app/create.tsx` (lines 314 + 324). Extracting it as a pure function would (a) DRY the two call sites onto one helper, (b) let a future "skip a color already used elsewhere in the collection" smart-pick swap in without touching the JSX, (c) earn a unit test that pins the rotation behaviour (today untested). Mirrors the `lib/uuid.ts` carve-out pattern.

- **Add an `AMBER_MUTED` family palette test** that asserts the 6-tier (`AMBER_MUTED` → `AMBER_MUTED_6`) lineage is monotonically lighter on the L axis of HSL space — today the lineage is named by index but a future "AMBER_MUTED_7 = #fff000" addition would silently break the visual ladder. A 15-line test using a `hexToHslLightness(hex): number` helper would enforce `L_n < L_{n+1}` across all 6 tiers. Same shape applies to `DANGER_DEEP_*` (5 tiers) and `MUTED_*` (21 tiers) — semantic ordering checks are cheap.

- **Generate a runtime-introspectable "tag swatch preview" gated behind `__DEV__`** at `app/_dev/tag-colors.tsx` rendering each of the 10 `TAG_COLORS` as a labelled chip alongside a sample "Rare" / "Limited" / "Vintage" tag label. Pairs naturally with the existing pending suggestion ("Generate a Storybook-style 'tokens preview' route at `app/_dev/tokens.tsx`") and gives designers a way to vet the categorical palette without spinning up the full create-item screen with 10 sample tags.


### app/collection/[id].tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Consolidate `MUTED_22 = "#6b4d35"` and `MUTED_23 = "#6a4d35"` into one token** — they're 1 byte apart on the red channel (same visual color to the human eye). The collection-detail file uses them as `bulkBarButtonGhost.borderColor` and `modalCancelText.color` respectively; merging onto a single `MUTED_22` would close a likely typo-origin lineage without any visual regression. Cheap palette-consolidation pass; pair with an HSL-distance test that flags any two tokens within `< 1% ΔE`.

- **Extract the `loadMore` + `loadMoreText` style pair into a reusable `<LoadMoreButton>` component** under `components/load-more-button.tsx` — the same styles + onPress + accessibility shape will likely repeat once the in-collection search/sort gets its own paginated child surface (and any future "Load more" on chats / marketplace / wishlist). The migration already centralized the colors; lifting the JSX closes the duplication before it spreads.

- **Add a structural test asserting `app/collection/[id].tsx` has no top-level `Object.freeze(...)` palette re-declaration** — now that the design-tokens migration is "fully proven", a future contributor refactoring the file might be tempted to re-declare a local palette object. The codebase's convention is `lib/design-tokens.ts` is the single source of truth; a grep-style guard (`assert.equal(src.match(/Object\.freeze/g)?.length ?? 0, 0)`) closes the regression vector.

- **Generate a token-usage heatmap script `scripts/token-usage-report.ts`** that scans `app/**/*.tsx` + `components/**/*.tsx` for each `lib/design-tokens.ts` export and prints a histogram of usage counts. Today nothing tells you that `BORDER` is used 47x while `MUTED_23` is used 1x — a usage report would surface candidates for the next palette-consolidation pass (e.g. promote single-use tokens into their files, or flag tokens with `0` uses as dead weight).

- **Add an HSL-axis monotonicity test for the `MUTED_*` family** — `MUTED_1` through `MUTED_23` is now a 23-tier lineage but the index order doesn't guarantee any visual ordering. A 20-line test using `hexToHslLightness(hex): number` would assert one of the axes (lightness, saturation, or hue) is monotonic across the index — surfacing accidental "MUTED_24 = #ff0000" additions that break the naming convention's implicit semantics. Same shape works for `TEXT_ON_DARK_*` (9 tiers), `DANGER_DEEP_*` (6 tiers), `CARD_BG_*` (13 tiers).

### components/qr-code.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Accept design-token names (not raw strings) in `QrCodeProps.color/background`** — today the prop is typed as `string`. Typing it as `DesignToken | (string & {})` (the established `(string & {})` trick already pending in `.tasks.md`) would give consumers autocomplete + typo-detection on the common path while still accepting any raw color string for one-off uses. Pairs with the existing pending `BackgroundColorValue/ColorValue` type-narrowing task.

- **Cache the `QRCode.create(value, ...)` matrix** across renders for the same `value` — today every `useMemo` walks the full library encode on each new `value`. A `WeakMap<string, boolean[][]>` keyed by value would close the gap for re-render heavy screens (e.g. the share sheet that re-renders the QR on every keystroke in the link field). Cheap optimisation matching the same memoization-by-key pattern already used elsewhere.

- **Add a structural test asserting `components/qr-code.tsx` exports the `QrCode` function with default `color`/`background` that resolve to design tokens** (not raw hex). Today the new adoption test only checks for the absence of inline hex; a stronger contract test would `import { QrCode } from "@/components/qr-code"` and assert the function signature carries `color = HERO_DARK, background = PURE_WHITE` via source-scan. Closes the regression vector where a future refactor could re-introduce a raw default while keeping the tokens imported elsewhere.

- **Promote the `QRCode.create` `errorCorrectionLevel: "M"` literal into a named constant** (`QR_ERROR_CORRECTION_LEVEL = "M"`) at module scope so a future "Q" or "H" upgrade for high-density QR data is a one-line edit. Today the literal lives inside the `useMemo` callback — fine for one consumer, but the share-sheet QR has data lengths that vary widely (deep-link → ~80 chars vs. UUID payloads → 36 chars), and the right error-correction level depends on the cell density.

- **Add a "QR contrast guard" test** that asserts the default `color` and `background` produce sufficient WCAG contrast (≥ 4.5:1) so a future palette swap that pairs two similar-luminance tokens (e.g. `MUTED_22` on `MUTED_23`) doesn't silently produce an un-scannable QR. A 20-line test using a `relativeLuminance(hex): number` helper + the WCAG ratio formula would close the regression vector for free.

### components/crash-fallback.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Consolidate `MUTED_24 = "#8a705a"` with `MUTED_7 = "#856d5a"`** — they're 4 channel bytes apart, visually indistinguishable to most users. The crash-fallback uses MUTED_24 once; if there's no design intent behind the slight difference, merging onto MUTED_7 would shrink the palette. Pair with an HSL-distance audit that flags any two MUTED_* tokens within ΔE < 2.

- **Add a per-file Sentry breadcrumb in `components/crash-fallback.tsx`** — today the fallback renders the error message but doesn't add an "encountered crash UI" breadcrumb. Wiring `addBreadcrumb("CrashFallback rendered", { extra: { detail } })` from `lib/sentry.ts` would let Sentry traces show that the user actually saw the fallback (vs. silently recovered). Cheap one-liner.

- **Type the `t` prop in `CrashFallbackProps`** more strictly using the project's `TranslationKey` union from `lib/i18n-context.tsx` — today `t?: (key: string) => string` accepts any string. Narrowing to `t?: (key: keyof typeof FALLBACK_STRINGS | string) => string` would surface typos in the `pick(t, "crashFallbackXxx")` calls at compile time.

- **Add a structural test asserting `components/crash-fallback.tsx` never imports the full i18n context** — the entire point of the fallback is to render *even when* the provider tree has collapsed. A grep-style guard (`assert.equal(src.match(/useI18n/g)?.length ?? 0, 0)`) closes the regression vector where a future refactor accidentally couples the crash boundary to the broken provider.

- **Promote the `FALLBACK_STRINGS` literal into a `lib/crash-fallback-strings.ts` module** so the same English defaults can be reused by other crash boundaries (e.g. a future `<RootErrorBoundary>`). Today the constants are inlined in the component file — extracting them centralises the canonical English fallback copy and lets a structural test enforce that no other crash UI re-declares the strings.

### components/screen.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Promote the 3-stop `<LinearGradient colors={[CARD_BG_7, PAGE_BG_2, PAGE_BG_3]}>` array into a `PAGE_BG_GRADIENT` exported tuple from `lib/design-tokens.ts`** — today the gradient stops are reconstructed inline. A `const PAGE_BG_GRADIENT = [CARD_BG_7, PAGE_BG_2, PAGE_BG_3] as const` export would (a) DRY the array if a second screen ever wants the same page-bg, (b) let a structural test enforce that no other file constructs an ad-hoc gradient with different cream stops, and (c) make the gradient direction/intent visible to a designer reviewing the palette doc.

- **Wire `useResponsive()` into a project-wide `lib/responsive.ts` module** — today the hook lives in `components/screen.tsx` but a header pill, a modal sheet, or a chat composer all want the same `isMobile`/`isTablet`/`isDesktop` breakpoints. Hoisting it would let those consumers import without pulling in the `<Screen>` JSX boilerplate.

- **Add a memoized `WeakMap<...>` cache for `useResponsive()`'s `contentMaxWidth` math** — today every consumer renders the hook fresh and re-derives the value from `width`. A `useMemo` keyed by width would close the gap; the per-pixel allocation cost is invisible but a 60fps scroll on a low-end Android hits the hook 60×/s.

- **Add a structural test asserting the `Screen` component's `staticInnerStyle` always includes `styles.fillContent`** — today the `scroll=false` branch depends on this for nested FlatList virtualization to size its viewport. A regression that drops the `flex: 1` would silently produce zero-height lists on every viewer-FlatList migration so far (VM-D). A 5-line source-scan guard would close the regression vector.

- **Type the `Screen.children` prop more strictly** — today `PropsWithChildren` accepts anything. Narrowing to `ReactNode` and adding a runtime warning when more than one root child is passed without a parent View would surface common Screen-misuse patterns (e.g. accidentally passing 2 sibling FlatLists, which the parent ScrollView can't size correctly).

### components/realtime-status-pill.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Consolidate `MUTED_25 = "#7a4d18"` with `MUTED_12 = "#7a4f1a"`** — these are 1-byte siblings (same shade to the human eye). The MUTED_22/_23 1-byte pair was also flagged for consolidation; if there's no design intent behind the small diff, merging onto MUTED_12 would shrink the palette. Pair with an HSL-distance audit that flags any two MUTED_* tokens within ΔE < 2.

- **Add an "online" + "offline" pill variant to `RealtimeStatusPill`** — today the pill only renders for `connecting` (mid-transition). A green "online" variant (using `STATUS_ONLINE`) shown briefly after reconnect would close the loop visually; an explicit "offline" variant (using `STATUS_OFFLINE`) shown after a connection timeout would distinguish "trying" from "gave up". Both fit on the existing pill chrome.

- **Wire the existing `useOptionalRealtimeStatus()` into a structural test that asserts the pill returns `null` outside the provider** — today the early-return is intentional but untested. A short unit test using a render-time check would close the regression vector against a future refactor that switches to `useRealtimeStatus()` (which throws outside the provider, crashing every screen that mounts the pill).

- **Add an `accessibilityRole="alert" + accessibilityLiveRegion="polite"` to the pill** so screen readers announce the connection state change. Today the pill is mute to assistive tech; a single prop change would close the a11y gap with zero design impact.

- **Make the pill text translatable via a `connectingPill` key instead of reusing `chatOfflinePill`** — today the pill reads "Offline · reconnecting" (the chat-specific copy) even when shown on marketplace/profile screens. A neutral "Reconnecting…" string would fit better across contexts; the chat module can keep the old key for its own banner.

### components/skeleton.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Promote `BASE_COLOR` and `HIGHLIGHT` into a named `SKELETON_BASE` + `SKELETON_HIGHLIGHT` pair in `lib/design-tokens.ts`** — today `HIGHLIGHT` is a raw `rgba(...)` string and `BASE_COLOR` is just a local alias for `TEXT_ON_DARK_SOFT`. If a future `<Skeleton variant="dark">` is added, both surfaces would benefit from canonical semantic names instead of re-deriving alpha from the cream palette. Pair with the planned `OVERLAY_*` family + `withAlpha()` helper so the `rgba(255, 250, 244, 0.9)` literal becomes `withAlpha(PAGE_BG_2, 0.9)`.

- **Memoize the `Animated.Value(0)` ref + the `loop.start()` effect with a stable dep** — today every Skeleton instance allocates a fresh `Animated.Value` even if it remounts with the same key. A `useRef(() => new Animated.Value(0))` lazy-init + a `useMemo` around the interpolation tuple would skip allocations for the 60-skeleton SkeletonProfileList burst. The win is invisible on desktop but ~2-3ms per remount on a low-end Android.

- **Add a `<SkeletonItemCard>` variant matching the `ItemCard compact` layout** — today the SkeletonCollectionDetail wraps a generic row-skeleton, but the viewer-FlatList branch in `app/collection/[id].tsx` mounts `<ItemCard compact />` cards. A purpose-built skeleton that mirrors the masonry cell shape would prevent a layout shift when the real cards swap in (the row layout currently jumps from ~80px row → ~220px card).

- **Hoist the local `styles.card` block into a shared `lib/skeleton-styles.ts` module** — the same `backgroundColor: PAGE_BG_2 + borderColor: BORDER_2 + radius: 20 + padding: 18` chrome appears in multiple skeleton variants and in real `<ItemCard>` / `<CollectionCard>` files. Centralizing would let a future card-radius/padding tweak propagate without grepping every skeleton variant.

- **Add a `reducedMotion` gate that disables the `Animated.loop`** when `AccessibilityInfo.isReduceMotionEnabled()` is true. Today the shimmer animation runs unconditionally, which is a documented a11y nausea trigger for vestibular-disorder users. A 5-line `useEffect` + state hook would stop the loop when the OS-level reduced-motion flag is on without changing the static placeholder appearance.

### app/collections-feed.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Hoist the `hero` chrome (`backgroundColor: HERO_DARK + borderRadius: 32 + padding: 24 + gap: 10`) into a `<HeroCard>` component** — the same 4-property block recurs across `app/index.tsx`, `app/wishlist.tsx`, `app/people.tsx`, and now `app/collections-feed.tsx`. A shared component would also let the eyebrow+title+subtitle chrome migrate together (today every screen rolls its own 3-text-block hero); centralizing would shrink each consumer to a `<HeroCard eyebrow={...} title={...} subtitle={...}>` 3-prop call.

- **Promote the `eyebrow`/`title`/`subtitle` typography triplet into a shared `lib/text-styles.ts` module** — today the same `textTransform: "uppercase" + letterSpacing: 1.2 + fontWeight: "800"` eyebrow shape repeats across 6+ screens, and the title's `fontSize: 28 + fontWeight: "800" + lineHeight: 36` also recurs. A `HERO_EYEBROW` / `HERO_TITLE` / `HERO_SUBTITLE` exported StyleSheet entry would let each screen reuse the typography without re-deriving.

- **Pin a structural test asserting the dark-hero text colors stay on the `TEXT_ON_DARK_*` family** — today nothing prevents a future contributor from picking `TEXT_DARK` (dark brown text on dark brown hero = invisible) for the title/subtitle. A grep-style guard like "if a file declares `backgroundColor: HERO_DARK`, every nested `color:` must come from the `TEXT_ON_DARK*` namespace" would catch the contrast regression at PR time.

- **Add an `accessibilityRole="header"` to the `hero` View** so screen readers announce it as a section heading rather than a generic group. Today the `<Text style={styles.title}>` is rendered without semantic structure; the eyebrow+title pair could also share a `accessibilityLabel` that combines both into one announcement instead of two.

- **Wire `feedCollectionsItemCounts` into a memoized `useItemCountsBatch(collections)` hook** — today the `useEffect` re-fires whenever `friendCollections` or `subscribedCollections` change identity (which happens on every social-context re-render). A hook keyed by stable collection IDs (rather than the full collection objects) would skip the redundant `Promise.all(fetchItemsByCollectionId(...))` round-trip when only the title/visibility of a collection changes — useful for the Supabase free-tier rate limits.

### app/auth/callback.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Hoist the `<ActivityIndicator size="large" color={ACCENT_DEEP}>` shape into a `<BrandSpinner>` component** — today the same accent-brown spinner color appears across 6+ screens (callback, marketplace loading, profile fetch, friend pull-to-refresh). A 5-line wrapper would mean a future "loading spinner" rebrand is a one-line edit, and the test surface shrinks from N adoption tests to one.

- **Replace the inline `try/catch` exchange-code/token-hash branch chain with a `lib/auth-callback.ts:resolveAuthFromUrl(url)` pure helper** — today the 50-line useEffect mixes URL parsing, three branch arms, and Supabase calls. Extracting the URL parsing into a `parseCallbackUrl(url): { kind: "tokens" | "code" | "tokenHash" | "error", ... }` discriminated union would let the screen be a thin "show working / show error / replace route" wrapper and let the helper be unit-tested without mocking the Supabase client.

- **Add an analytics event `auth_callback_error` keyed by the discriminated `errorCode` from the URL hash** — today errors are surfaced to the user but not captured. Pairing it with the existing `authClient` event taxonomy would surface "Google OAuth flow gives `access_denied` 30% of the time" patterns that today are invisible because they fail silently outside the Supabase dashboard.

- **Wire the `cancelled` flag through a more idiomatic `AbortController`** — today the `cancelled` boolean is a one-off pattern; the rest of the codebase uses `AbortController`/`signal` for cancellation. Standardising would make the cleanup pattern legible to any reader and skip the (rare) race where `setError` fires after the useEffect returns its cleanup function.

- **Surface the error message in the OS error reporter (Sentry)** — today the user sees the error text but `lib/sentry.ts:captureException` isn't called. A 2-line `captureException(nextError instanceof Error ? nextError : new Error(...), { tags: { surface: "auth_callback" } })` would log every callback failure with full stack to the diagnostics backend, gated by the existing `DiagnosticsProvider` opt-out so it respects user consent.

### components/collection-card.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Delete the unused `role` StyleSheet entry** — declared on line 82 but never referenced in JSX (the `<View style={styles.topRow}>` block uses `<VisibilityBadge>` instead, which has its own internal "role"/visibility chrome). Dead style entries add noise and produce false positives in the adoption test's "expected token names" list. A one-line removal would also slim the file by ~7 lines.

- **Audit the 5 new `TEXT_ON_DARK_10..13` + `MUTED_26` tokens for cross-file reuse** — these were added because no existing palette entry came within ΔE<3 of the inline literals, but the same warm-cream shades may appear in `components/item-card.tsx` (still pending migration) or in marketing-style heroes in `app/index.tsx`. A bulk grep-then-consolidate pass after the design-tokens sweep completes would shrink the `TEXT_ON_DARK_*` family from 13 entries back to ~6 by retiring near-duplicates onto a single canonical value.

- **Promote the `rgba(34, 24, 17, 0.36)` overlay into a `HERO_OVERLAY` token + `withAlpha(HERO_DARK, 0.36)` helper** — today this is the second `rgba(...)` literal that the 6-digit regex can't catch, after the rgba in `components/skeleton.tsx`. Centralizing both alpha overlays under the planned `OVERLAY_*` family (with a typed `withAlpha(token: DesignToken, alpha: number)` helper) would close the alpha-shade migration gap that 6+ pending files all carry.

- **Add a structural test asserting collection-card text contrast against the `MUTED_26` fallback bg** — today `MUTED_26 = #c8b8a4` is the warm tan-grey bg shown when there's no cover. The text colors are tuned for the dark-image-with-overlay case; on the bare fallback bg, the white title + cream text may fail WCAG AA contrast. A computed-contrast test or a documented "use shaded variant when no cover" comment would close the a11y regression vector.

- **Wire `<CollectionCard>` through the existing `Skeleton` placeholder** while the cover image is loading — today the `<Image>` mounts directly with no loading state, so a cold network produces a brief flash of `MUTED_26` warm-grey before the photo paints. A 5-line `useState(false) + onLoad → setLoaded(true)` gate + `<Skeleton style={StyleSheet.absoluteFillObject}>` overlay during the loading window would smooth the cold-load UX without changing the warm-state appearance.

### components/selectable-item-row.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Hoist the `<Pressable>` + checkbox overlay shape into a generic `<SelectableRow>` component** in `components/selectable-row.tsx` — today selectable-item-row is item-specific (`<ItemCard>` inside) but the same Pressable+checkbox+borderRadius+accent-border pattern is needed for `<SelectableCollectionRow>` and a future `<SelectableContactRow>` (bulk friend-actions). A generic component taking a `children` slot would let three+ call sites share the chrome.

- **Replace the inline `selected ? <Text>✓</Text> : null` with an `Ionicons` checkmark** to match the rest of the app's icon system (the codebase uses `@expo/vector-icons` Ionicons for every other checkmark — see `app/create.tsx`, `app/item/[id].tsx`). A `name="checkmark"` Ionicons would also scale crisp at any pixel density (the current Text-based glyph relies on the system font's "✓" character which varies across iOS/Android/web).
