- **Add an `accessibilityRole="checkbox" + accessibilityState={{ checked: selected }}`** to the outer Pressable so screen readers announce "checkbox, checked"/"checkbox, not checked" instead of the generic "button". The checkbox semantic is the correct WAI-ARIA role for a multi-select toggle. Single-prop addition with zero design impact.

- **Tune the React.memo's compare function** with an explicit `(prev, next) => prev.selected === next.selected && prev.item === next.item && prev.onToggle === next.onToggle` instead of the default shallow compare. Today the default works because all 3 props are scalar/reference-identity-stable, but pinning the comparator makes the perf invariant explicit and surfaces any future prop additions that need their own equality strategy.

- **Add a structural test asserting the `SelectableItemRow` Pressable doesn't nest inside another Pressable** — today the row is rendered standalone in selection mode, but a future "tap-to-expand row + select sub-checkbox" layout would create nested Pressables (React Native warns about this). A grep-style guard that the row's outer is always a direct FlatList child would close the regression vector.

### components/reaction-bar.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Inline the unused `REACTION_EMOJIS` import** — `components/reaction-bar.tsx` line 4 pulls `REACTION_EMOJIS` from `@/lib/use-reactions` but never references it; only `useReactions` is consumed. A 1-token grep+removal keeps the import surface honest and pairs with the eslint `no-unused-vars` rule already in `eslint.config.js`. The lint guardrail would catch the regression that a future contributor reintroduces a dead import.

- **Promote chipActive's identical bg+border to a single `chipActiveSurface` style entry** — today `chipActive.backgroundColor = HERO_DARK` and `chipActive.borderColor = HERO_DARK` repeat the same token, which means a future "change the active chip accent to AMBER_ACCENT" tweak requires editing two lines instead of one. A `backgroundColor: HERO_DARK, borderColor: HERO_DARK` pattern recurs in 5+ other StyleSheets (`components/selectable-item-row.tsx`, `app/chats.tsx`, etc.); a shared `surface(token)` style helper that returns `{ backgroundColor: token, borderColor: token }` would dedupe the pattern across the codebase.

- **Add an `accessibilityRole="button" + accessibilityState={{ selected: item.mine }}`** to each reaction chip Pressable so screen readers announce "heart reaction, selected"/"thumbs-up reaction, not selected" instead of the generic Pressable announcement. Today the chip just reads as a tap target with no semantic context. Mirrors the same pattern listed for `<SelectableItemRow>` — apply both in one a11y pass.

- **Wire the reaction toggle through an optimistic-update pattern** — today `void toggle(item.key)` fires-and-forgets, and the UI doesn't reflect the new count until `useReactions` re-fetches. A `useOptimistic` (or manual `setLocalCounts`) layer would let the chip count tick up/down instantly on tap, then reconcile when the cloud confirms. The latency hit is invisible on a fast network but stark on slow connections — RX-friendly UX for free.

- **Add a "long-press chip to see reactor names" affordance** — the existing `useReactions` hook already knows which user IDs reacted (it computes `mine` from `userId`), so wiring a long-press handler that opens a `<Sheet>` with the user list would surface "who liked this" without a new endpoint. Mirrors Instagram/Telegram reaction UX, makes the social signal much richer than just the count.

### components/photo-preview.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Migrate the three `rgba(38, 27, 20, 0.x)` + `rgba(141, 43, 43, 0.8)` overlay literals into a shared `OVERLAY_*` family** — `photo-preview.tsx` carries 3 distinct alpha overlays (`0.6`, `0.7`, `0.8`) all keyed off either `HERO_DARK = #261b14` (= `rgb(38, 27, 20)`) or `DANGER_DEEP = #8d2b2b` (= `rgb(141, 43, 43)`). Today the 6-digit regex doesn't catch them so the adoption test passes, but a future `withAlpha(HERO_DARK, 0.7)` helper would dedupe these across 6+ files (`photo-preview`, `skeleton`, `collection-card`, ...) and unblock the design-tokens "alpha shade" gap that's been mentioned in 4+ prior suggestions.

- **Replace the inline `<Ionicons name="chevron-back" />` / `<Ionicons name="chevron-forward" />` button content with `<ChevronButton direction="back|forward">`** — today both move buttons hand-roll the same `Pressable` + `Ionicons` + `hitSlop={4}` + `styles.moveButton` chrome, with the only difference being the icon name and the move target. A 20-line `<ChevronButton>` extraction would dedupe the pair and give the codebase a reusable left/right paginator for other grid-reorder UIs (`app/profile/edit-photos.tsx`, the avatar reorder sheet, etc.).

- **Promote `removePhoto`+`movePhoto` into a `usePhotoOrdering(photos, onChange)` hook** — the two handlers are pure transformations over the `photos` array with no React state, but they recreate the array via `filter` / `splice` on every render. A custom hook returning `{ removePhoto, movePhoto }` wrapped in `useCallback` would (a) stop the per-render allocation and (b) let `<PhotoPreview>` consumers (item-detail edit, profile edit, listing create) share the same logic for free.

- **Add a drag-to-reorder gesture wrapper** — today the only reordering affordance is the two chevron buttons, which means moving photo #5 to position #1 requires 4 taps. Wrapping `<View style={styles.item}>` in `<DraggableFlatList>` (already a dependency for `app/collection/[id].tsx` drag mode) would deliver a single-gesture reorder UX without changing the data contract.

- **Render a long-press preview / fullscreen viewer when a thumb is held** — the photo-preview is the only path users have to verify they uploaded the right images, but at 104×104 px a thumbnail is too small to spot a mis-cropped shot. A 30-line `<PhotoViewer>` modal that opens on long-press (mirroring `app/item/[id].tsx`'s lightbox) would let users sanity-check uploads before committing. The data is already in hand — only the modal scaffolding is missing.

### components/visibility-badge.tsx design-tokens migration (2026-05-25)

- **Inline the unused `FONT_BODY` import** — `components/visibility-badge.tsx` line 6 pulls `FONT_BODY` from `@/lib/fonts` but never references it; only `FONT_BODY_BOLD` is consumed across the 4 text variants. A 1-token removal would silence the `unused-vars` warning that the project's eslint config should be flagging.

- **Promote the 7 `rgba(...)` overlay literals into an `OVERLAY_*` family with `withAlpha(token, opacity)` helper** — `visibility-badge.tsx` has the densest concentration of `rgba(...)` literals in the codebase (7 in one file across 3 alpha tiers per variant × hero/card pair), each one tied to a specific named base color (`#4a7c59` viewer green, `#d89c5b` shared amber, `#6b5647` private muted, `#ffffff` hero white). A `withAlpha(SUCCESS_GREEN_2, 0.12)` / `withAlpha(AMBER_ACCENT, 0.15)` helper would dedupe all 7 onto 4 named base tokens × declared alphas, closing the rgba migration gap that's blocked 6+ files from achieving 100% adoption.

- **Extract the `isViewer ? ... : isShared ? ... : ...` 4-way ternary into a `getBadgeColors(state, variant)` helper** — today the same 4-way branch appears twice in the component: once in the `Ionicons color` prop and once spread across 4 StyleSheet entries (`badgeText` / `badgeTextHero` / `badgeTextViewer` / `badgeTextShared`). A single `getBadgeColors({ isViewer, isShared, isHero })` returning `{ icon, text }` would make the state→color mapping a one-line table instead of duplicate ternary chains.

- **Add an `accessibilityRole="text" + accessibilityLabel={`Visibility: ${label}`}`** to the outer `<View>` so screen readers announce the visibility state ("Visibility: private") instead of just the label text. Today the badge is a decorative icon+text pair with no a11y semantics; one prop closes the gap.

- **Wire the badge through `<Pressable onPress={openVisibilitySheet}>`** to make the chip itself a tappable affordance that opens the visibility-edit sheet (today the badge is purely display and the edit path is buried in collection-detail menus). Mirrors how Notion / Linear surface visibility-toggle as a directly-clickable chip — discoverability win for ~10 LOC.
